# Data Management Essential Training

> Looking for a crash course in data management? Look no further—this course is for you. Join database platform architect and Microsoft MVP Jess Pomfret as she provides a comprehensive overview of the complete data management lifecycle, from data acquisition and storage to data processing, governance, security, analysis, and more. Along the way, develop practical skills for implementing robust data 

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training) | 2h 49m | Beginner | 36K learners
> [Jump to Path Context ↓](#path-context)

>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-management?u=76281980&t=9)** I have decided to take us on a journey following the data management lifecycle.

>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-management?u=76281980&t=62)** You'll discover why each stage of the lifecycle is important, how to be successful, and any pitfalls to be aware of.

#### Benefits of effective data management
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/benefits-of-effective-data-management?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/benefits-of-effective-data-management?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Before we start on crafting the perfect data management strategy, it's important to work out why we are going through this effort.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/benefits-of-effective-data-management?u=76281980&t=7)** What are the benefits to our organizations of effectively managing our data?
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/benefits-of-effective-data-management?u=76281980&t=13)** The folks leading modern businesses are faced with making decisions all day, every day.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/benefits-of-effective-data-management?u=76281980&t=18)** In order to make the correct decision, they need all of the relevant information, and they need that information to be accurate, easy to find, and to make sense.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/benefits-of-effective-data-management?u=76281980&t=29)** The volume of data is ever increasing, and so the ability to make decisions based on raw numbers in a spreadsheet is a thing of the past.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/benefits-of-effective-data-management?u=76281980&t=38)** Instead, decision-makers rely on carefully designed data visualizations, pulling together multiple data sources into a single dashboard to enable them to make the most informed decision possible.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/benefits-of-effective-data-management?u=76281980&t=53)** But in order to create that perfect dashboard, we need to consider all the work that goes into getting data to that stage, and this is why an effective data management strategy is vital.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/benefits-of-effective-data-management?u=76281980&t=66)** One of the main benefits of data management is data accuracy.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/benefits-of-effective-data-management?u=76281980&t=70)** Even the best reports and dashboards are useless if the data isn't accurate.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/benefits-of-effective-data-management?u=76281980&t=75)** Implementing a good data management strategy will ensure that data is captured correctly, validated, and continually monitored throughout the processing stages to ensure that by the time it appears on our final reports, it remains error free.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/benefits-of-effective-data-management?u=76281980&t=92)** Now, data storage might not be the most thrilling topic, but it is critical.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/benefits-of-effective-data-management?u=76281980&t=97)** Knowing where the data is stored, that it is secure and safe builds an important foundation for all the processing and reporting that will be built on top of it.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/benefits-of-effective-data-management?u=76281980&t=109)** Winning at data storage can also provide cost savings, and what business doesn't love some cost savings?
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/benefits-of-effective-data-management?u=76281980&t=116)** Focus here is on ensuring only the necessary data is kept and that it is stored in a format that is both useful and cost effective.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/benefits-of-effective-data-management?u=76281980&t=125)** Also, only keeping the data you need ensures that you're meeting all data regulations and reducing the risk of having any compliance issues.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/benefits-of-effective-data-management?u=76281980&t=132)** Having data stored in an optimal fashion also increases data accessibility.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/benefits-of-effective-data-management?u=76281980&t=138)** It's not just the CEO that is making data-driven decisions.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/benefits-of-effective-data-management?u=76281980&t=143)** Accessibility also covers improving the ease of sharing the data between departments, enabling teams to work more effectively together.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/benefits-of-effective-data-management?u=76281980&t=153)** Finally, it's worth mentioning that most businesses have a goal of growth, more customers, more market share, and more data.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/benefits-of-effective-data-management?u=76281980&t=161)** Ensuring we have our data management dialed in means that scaling with this growth doesn't create pain points, but instead becomes a tool for success.

#### Data lifecycle management
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-lifecycle-management?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Data is vital for the businesses of today, which is why data management is so important.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=6)** And this management isn't a one step process, but more the care and feeding of this data as it travels into and throughout our business teams.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=16)** There is a lifecycle for data within our organizations, and this starts with the acquisition of data.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=22)** The first step is data collection.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=25)** Step one for doing anything with data is collecting it.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=30)** Getting it from the many disparate sources, such as point of sale systems or spreadsheets from different areas of the business, and ensuring it is collected in an effective manner that maintains the accuracy of the information.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=43)** No matter how good the rest of our data management strategy is, collecting inaccurate data will set us up for failure down the line.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=53)** The next stage in the lifecycle is data processing and integration.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=57)** The data we receive is in a raw format.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=60)** It could be sales data coming from our retail stores, or perhaps metrics coming from IoT devices in our warehouses.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=68)** This data probably needs to go through some transformation process, such as cleaning or aggregation, to get it into the most useful format.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=78)** Throughout this process though, we need to maintain the needed granularity, quality, and consistency of the data.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=86)** Once the data has been processed, we move on to step three, which is storage.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=91)** There are many options for storing data, from flat files all the way to data warehouses.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=96)** We'll cover each of these options in a later chapter.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=100)** The key here is matching the right data storage solution to the data, ensuring the data is both stored in a secure fashion and in a way that makes it easy to use.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=112)** Once our data has been stored, we can move on to data analysis.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=116)** This stage is where we start to pull out meaningful insights from our data.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=121)** This is usually carried out by data scientists, applying statistical models and complex computational techniques to look for patterns and derive findings from the data.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=132)** The final stage of this process involves presenting these findings, creating beautiful dashboards, visualizations, and graphics that enable business leaders to make decisions based on the data that has traversed this whole lifecycle.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=147)** Throughout this whole process are two wrappers, which are governance and artificial intelligence, or AI.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=154)** Governance ensures that our data is secure, remains accurate, and that we're complying with regulations.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=162)** AI is the new hot topic, but it can be very useful throughout all the stages of this data lifecycle.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=170)** AI can help us to improve automation and efficiency throughout the stages, meaning we can glean more insights and knowledge from the data we have collected, stored, and processed.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=182)** That wraps up the data management lifecycle.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=184)** You'll notice we keep coming back to this diagram as we progress through the course.

#### Key concepts in data management
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/key-concepts-in-data-management?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/key-concepts-in-data-management?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] As we've seen in the previous video which discussed the data management lifecycle, there is a lot to cover in this course, and so we need to start with a solid foundation of knowledge to build off.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/key-concepts-in-data-management?u=76281980&t=12)** This foundation will be the key concepts of data management.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/key-concepts-in-data-management?u=76281980&t=17)** There are a few key concepts that we will introduce in this video and we'll see them cropping up again throughout the rest of the chapters.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/key-concepts-in-data-management?u=76281980&t=25)** Understanding what these key concepts are will help us to piece together a full picture of the topic of data management.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/key-concepts-in-data-management?u=76281980&t=34)** Protecting our data has to be one of the most important concerns throughout this entire data management strategy.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/key-concepts-in-data-management?u=76281980&t=40)** In today's world, there are so many ways to fall victim to data security issues.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/key-concepts-in-data-management?u=76281980&t=46)** Keeping our data secure through all of the lifecycle steps will not only ensure the organization's good reputation is maintained, but will also ensure fines and penalties are avoided.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/key-concepts-in-data-management?u=76281980&t=58)** And let's be honest, a data security incident can cause enough financial hardship to put companies out of business.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/key-concepts-in-data-management?u=76281980&t=64)** Avoiding this is vital.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/key-concepts-in-data-management?u=76281980&t=68)** Data privacy goes hand in hand with security.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/key-concepts-in-data-management?u=76281980&t=71)** This relates to how we look after potentially sensitive data.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/key-concepts-in-data-management?u=76281980&t=75)** Is personally identifiable information or PII data masked or obfuscated in areas where we don't need it?
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/key-concepts-in-data-management?u=76281980&t=83)** Are we compliant with laws and regulations such as GDPR, which governs how long we can retain certain data?
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/key-concepts-in-data-management?u=76281980&t=92)** We also need to think about data reliability.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/key-concepts-in-data-management?u=76281980&t=95)** Whatever great insights our data scientists can glean from our data are only useful if they are founded from accurate and reliable data.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/key-concepts-in-data-management?u=76281980&t=104)** As we collect, store, and transform our data, we need to be mindful of this the whole time.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/key-concepts-in-data-management?u=76281980&t=112)** Next is accessibility.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/key-concepts-in-data-management?u=76281980&t=114)** This is also key throughout our organization.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/key-concepts-in-data-management?u=76281980&t=118)** Having this great data is only useful if it's easily available to those that need it.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/key-concepts-in-data-management?u=76281980&t=124)** We'll think about this concept during our storage chapter as this is a major consideration as we decide what the best storage medium is.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/key-concepts-in-data-management?u=76281980&t=135)** Finally, I want to mention scalability.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/key-concepts-in-data-management?u=76281980&t=138)** The data management strategy that we craft as we work through this course needs to be one that works now, but also has the ability to scale and work well in the future.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/key-concepts-in-data-management?u=76281980&t=149)** As our business grows, we will have a higher volume of data, but also potentially more and different data sources to integrate in.

#### Data quality assurance and data cleansing
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-quality-assurance-and-data-cleansing?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-quality-assurance-and-data-cleansing?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] I want to add a few points to why data quality is so important.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-quality-assurance-and-data-cleansing?u=76281980&t=5)** There are many options throughout the storage processing and presenting portions of our lifecycle to redo work or try something else.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-quality-assurance-and-data-cleansing?u=76281980&t=14)** You can always move data to a different storage solution or process and present it in a slightly different fashion, but if that data is inaccurate or of poor quality, it's hard to rectify that.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-quality-assurance-and-data-cleansing?u=76281980&t=28)** This is why it's worth it in the early stages to make sure that the data is accurately collected and of a high quality.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-quality-assurance-and-data-cleansing?u=76281980&t=35)** But what is high quality data?
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-quality-assurance-and-data-cleansing?u=76281980&t=38)** The first characteristic is accuracy, and it's probably what most of us would think about first.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-quality-assurance-and-data-cleansing?u=76281980&t=44)** This is that the data correctly represents what it describes in the real world, but it's also important to think of completeness.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-quality-assurance-and-data-cleansing?u=76281980&t=52)** This is that the data is fully captured, meaning that we didn't capture the event but miss the times stamp of its occurrence, for example.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-quality-assurance-and-data-cleansing?u=76281980&t=61)** Without complete data, it's much harder to draw those key insights later down the road.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-quality-assurance-and-data-cleansing?u=76281980&t=67)** The data should also be consistent.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-quality-assurance-and-data-cleansing?u=76281980&t=70)** We all know that you can't compare apples and oranges, so ensuring we collect data in the same uniform way means that we can easily make comparisons and aggregate the data into meaningful shapes.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-quality-assurance-and-data-cleansing?u=76281980&t=82)** We can also think about timeliness.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-quality-assurance-and-data-cleansing?u=76281980&t=85)** This is particularly important if we're thinking about real-time data and making decisions on data close to the occurrence.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-quality-assurance-and-data-cleansing?u=76281980&t=94)** Having a way to quickly collect store and process the data into reports that can drive decisions can be vital for some fast-paced industries.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-quality-assurance-and-data-cleansing?u=76281980&t=103)** Finally, data uniqueness should also be considered.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-quality-assurance-and-data-cleansing?u=76281980&t=107)** This is that we only collect each data point.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-quality-assurance-and-data-cleansing?u=76281980&t=109)** One time reducing storage size and costs from storing duplicate data that isn't needed.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-quality-assurance-and-data-cleansing?u=76281980&t=118)** It's worth spending a little extra time upfront for these considerations as if you get to the end of the process and realize the data quality is poor.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-quality-assurance-and-data-cleansing?u=76281980&t=126)** It'll be really hard work to unpick the process and basically start over again.

>

>

>

>

>

>

>

>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/common-challenges-in-data-management?u=76281980&t=123)** If our company is breached, not only can it cost money in fines and work to rebuild any affected machines, it can also cost our reputation.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/common-challenges-in-data-management?u=76281980&t=132)** Customers trust is vitally important, and we want to ensure we're doing everything we can to keep their data from ending up on the dark web.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Definitions:** is an  (1), means that (1), is a  (1)

#### Types of data sources
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] In today's world, data is everywhere, and our aim in this chapter is to decide what to collect and how to collect it.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=7)** So first things first, let's think about what kind of data sources we have available to us and some examples of each kind.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=14)** Remember, this is not an exhaustive list.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=17)** There will be data in your environments that I don't specifically mention in this course that will be really useful to collect and involve in your strategy.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=25)** The first type of data for us to consider is structured data.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=29)** As you can perhaps guess from the title, this is data that is already structured into rows and columns.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=34)** This could be stored within spreadsheets or databases.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=38)** Some examples of structured data sources to consider would be customer relationship management, or CRM systems, enterprise resource planning, or ERP systems, and other transactional databases, such as those using MySQL or Microsoft SQL Server to store data.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=56)** We also have unstructured data sources to consider when collecting data.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=59)** This is the exact opposite of our structured data, and includes text, images and videos.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=66)** These data sources might include emails, social media interactions, and video or audio recordings.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=72)** This data can't be stored in a relational database, but can still provide important insights such as customer sentiment or market trends.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=80)** I like to think of data sources as a spectrum.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=83)** On one end, we have very structured sources, like our ERP or CRM systems, and then on the other end, we have very unstructured sources, like our social media interactions or customer reviews.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=95)** In between both ends of the spectrum, we have a third category of data sources we'll call semi-structured.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=102)** These data sources include server logs, API responses, and output from IoT devices.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=109)** This data has some structure and is often in XML or JSON formats, but it's not as rigid as data stored within relational databases.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=118)** Outside of this spectrum, we also have two other categories of data sources to consider.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=123)** The first being real-time data.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=126)** Again, IoT data would fall into this category.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=129)** This is data that has been streamed in real time from machines in our manufacturing facilities, or maybe telemetry information from our fleet of delivery vehicles.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=138)** There is also some industry-related, real-time data that may be applicable such as financial market information, like real-time trades and stock prices, or in the healthcare field, patient monitoring devices streaming vital signs that could predict imminent medical issues.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=155)** The final category of data sources to consider are third-party sources.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=159)** We can use these sources to augment the data we currently collected from our internal sources.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=166)** One of my favorite examples of a third-party data source is around ice cream sales.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=171)** As you can imagine, sales vary widely from day to day, which makes forecasting difficult.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=176)** How will we know how much ice cream we need to have available to when there is so much variance?
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=181)** Some days in June, we sell 100 units, while other days in June, we only sell 10 units.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=188)** Well, if we integrate weather data, we might be able to see that on the day we sold 100 units, it was hot and sunny, whereas the day we only sold 10 units, it rained all day.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=198)** Now we can start to see patterns and more easily predict how many units will sell on a given day.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=204)** Adding in third-party weather data allows the ice cream store to better understand the fluctuation in units sold.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=211)** Another common third-party data source is census information.
>
> **[3:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=215)** This provides information on the population, which could help businesses to decide where to expand or determine which products do well in which areas.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=225)** As you can see, there is a wide variety of potentially helpful data sources out there.
>
> **[3:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=230)** Have a think about your specific organization and industry and begin pulling together a list of data sources that you believe will be helpful in driving future business decisions.
>
> **[4:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-sources?u=76281980&t=240)** Now you're on your way to planning an effective data management strategy.

#### Data collection methods
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-collection-methods?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-collection-methods?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] All right.
>
> **[0:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-collection-methods?u=76281980&t=1)** In the previous video, we covered what data sources we have available to us, and the next step is to talk about how to collect that data.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-collection-methods?u=76281980&t=7)** How we collect data varies wildly from each type of data source that we have available to us.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-collection-methods?u=76281980&t=12)** But before we do that, let's talk through a few of the data sources we have discussed already.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-collection-methods?u=76281980&t=18)** Let's start by thinking about some of our structured data sources.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-collection-methods?u=76281980&t=21)** These systems collect data through applications.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-collection-methods?u=76281980&t=24)** For example, the transaction database for sales data will be populated from the application used to make sales.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-collection-methods?u=76281980&t=30)** The source may come right from the till used by the cashiers in our stores.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-collection-methods?u=76281980&t=35)** There are other data sources where data is captured in an automated fashion.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-collection-methods?u=76281980&t=39)** These include IOT sensors.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-collection-methods?u=76281980&t=41)** This type of data is streamed straight from the devices.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-collection-methods?u=76281980&t=45)** Some data can only be collected in a more manual fashion, but can still provide great insights, so it's still worth considering in our overall strategy.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-collection-methods?u=76281980&t=54)** This often includes things like surveys or focus groups.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-collection-methods?u=76281980&t=58)** Collecting this data can be time consuming, but that type of information can be an invaluable source.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-collection-methods?u=76281980&t=66)** Data can also be collected through APIs.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-collection-methods?u=76281980&t=68)** This stands for application programming interfaces.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-collection-methods?u=76281980&t=72)** APIs enable easy integration with third party data sources.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-collection-methods?u=76281980&t=76)** APIs could be used to collect weather data, social media data, financial market stats, and much more.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-collection-methods?u=76281980&t=88)** Here you can see a simple call to a weather, API to get the current weather forecast for a certain latitude and longitude.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-collection-methods?u=76281980&t=94)** In this case, it's for Carpenteria, California where we're recording this course right now.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-collection-methods?u=76281980&t=99)** Also, we start to see a lot of companies using software as a service or SaaS providers.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-collection-methods?u=76281980&t=105)** Data from these can also be accessed via API and integrated into our data sources and eventually into our reports.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-collection-methods?u=76281980&t=111)** There is no golden rule on how to collect data from the many sources you have available to you.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-collection-methods?u=76281980&t=116)** But with this information, you should start to be able to gather together the required tools and strategies.

#### Efficient data management with data sampling
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/efficient-data-management-with-data-sampling?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/efficient-data-management-with-data-sampling?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] As we've seen in the last couple of videos, there are a lot of data sources to consider and a lot of ways to collect data.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/efficient-data-management-with-data-sampling?u=76281980&t=6)** All of this combines to create a huge volume of data.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/efficient-data-management-with-data-sampling?u=76281980&t=9)** In some cases, we need to use data sampling to help improve the efficiency of our process.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/efficient-data-management-with-data-sampling?u=76281980&t=15)** Data sampling is the process where you select a representative subset of data to speed up our ability to process the data and enable faster, but still accurate insights.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/efficient-data-management-with-data-sampling?u=76281980&t=26)** There are several techniques we can consider to create this subset of data.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/efficient-data-management-with-data-sampling?u=76281980&t=30)** First, we could choose random sampling.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/efficient-data-management-with-data-sampling?u=76281980&t=32)** This is, as it sounds, a random selection of the data is analyzed.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/efficient-data-management-with-data-sampling?u=76281980&t=36)** This is useful for certain data sources where we want to ensure we remove any selection bias, such as surveys or questionnaires.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/efficient-data-management-with-data-sampling?u=76281980&t=44)** Our second technique is stratified sampling.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/efficient-data-management-with-data-sampling?u=76281980&t=47)** For this data, you divide the dataset into strata or segments based on specific characteristics, and then draw random samples from each of the segments.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/efficient-data-management-with-data-sampling?u=76281980&t=56)** This is important where there are certain subsets of the data that need to be represented, but you still want to select randomly.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/efficient-data-management-with-data-sampling?u=76281980&t=64)** Finally, we could use systematic sampling where we choose a random starting spot in the dataset, but then choose every "nth" member of that dataset.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/efficient-data-management-with-data-sampling?u=76281980&t=72)** This is often used for quality control type work as you just want to check in on certain data points.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/efficient-data-management-with-data-sampling?u=76281980&t=80)** These techniques come from statistics and can get quite complicated.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/efficient-data-management-with-data-sampling?u=76281980&t=83)** In fact, there are whole courses in the LinkedIn Learning library that dive into these sampling techniques in more detail if you're interested.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/efficient-data-management-with-data-sampling?u=76281980&t=91)** Anyway, this gives you an idea of how using data sampling can help to reduce the amount of data you're dealing with while maintaining the integrity of the dataset.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/efficient-data-management-with-data-sampling?u=76281980&t=99)** By trimming down the size, we get benefits such as cost saving and as mentioned earlier, we can access insights quicker, which can make all the difference as folks can more rapidly make business decisions from our implemented data sets.

>
> **CLI Commands:** make (2)
> **Code Keywords:** finally, (1)
> **Cross-References:** in the last (1)

#### Data validation: Ensuring accurate data
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] Another important concept I want to cover while we're talking about data collection is data validation.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=5)** We're early in our data management lifecycle at this point, and it's vital that at this stage we make sure we have accurate data.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=11)** Without accurate data now, the rest of the lifecycle is worthless, which means there won't be a solid foundation for sound business decisions.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=19)** The easiest way for me to illustrate data validation is when I think about filling in a form online.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=24)** There are several fields where we must enter information.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=27)** It's likely the form is using validation techniques to ensure we enter the correct information.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=33)** There are several different techniques that can be used here.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=36)** First, there are format checks.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=38)** The easiest example here is an email address.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=41)** We know that email addresses need to be formatted in a certain way to be valid.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=45)** They need to be a string followed by an at symbol, another string, a full stop or period, and then another string.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=51)** There is some variability in the end of email addresses.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=54)** For example, both ".com" and ".co.uk" are valid.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=58)** So when we're adding data validation, we need to ensure it allows all possibilities.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=65)** We could also use data type and range checks.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=68)** Perhaps we ask for the numbers of years a person has lived at their current address.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=72)** We can specify that the data type must be an integer, and we could add the range of something like zero to 120.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=79)** So unrealistic values can't be added.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=83)** Finally, we could compare multiple fields to make use of crossfield validation.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=87)** This would ensure that if we require a start date and an end date, that the end date is after the start date.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=93)** These all seem like quite straightforward concepts, but the more guardrails we can add around any data entry and data collection, the more likely we are to get accurate, complete, and reliable data.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=104)** Another part of ensuring we have accurate data is looking for and removing any duplicates.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=110)** Having duplicates not only reduces data quality, which can ruin our metrics and analysis, but it also causes operational inefficiencies like having more data to store and process, which increases costs and processing duration.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=125)** To identify duplicates, we can either use unique identifiers data, which should be unique for each row in our dataset, such as customer IDs or product SKUs.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=135)** Or if we don't have a way of uniquely identifying each record, we can use some matching techniques.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=140)** These can be a little tricky, but the goal is to find data that is likely the same.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=145)** For example, maybe I've entered my information four times as Mrs. Pomfret, J. Pomfret, Jess Pomfret, or maybe even incorrectly spelled.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=155)** There really is only one of me, so I would want all of my orders, for example, to be grouped together.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=161)** But if I've entered my name differently each time, they might not be being able to work out that these are in fact duplicates can help clean up our data and keep it accurate.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=172)** It's important to note that this isn't a one-time activity.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=174)** As data is added over time, it's important to continuously look for new duplicates to resolve.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-validation-ensuring-accurate-data?u=76281980&t=180)** Using all of these techniques will ensure that our data is accurate, reliable, and complete, which means we'll be in great shape to continue moving on through the data management lifecycle.

>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-acquisition-best-practices?u=76281980&t=9)** Let's go over some best practices that you can think about as you work through this phase in your own organizations.

>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-acquisition-best-practices?u=76281980&t=26)** The more data we collect, the more there is to process and store, which makes the process more difficult and the resource cost higher.
>

>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-acquisition-best-practices?u=76281980&t=49)** Without accurate, complete, reliable data, the end result of all this work will not be worth it because we won't be able to make sound business decisions off of the data.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-acquisition-best-practices?u=76281980&t=59)** Spending time on data accuracy and integrity will set us up for success moving forward.

>

>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-acquisition-best-practices?u=76281980&t=75)** This is particularly important if we're pulling in third party data.
>

>

#### Challenges in data collection
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-collection?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-collection?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] Well folks, it's time to talk about some of the challenges that we might face in this data collection stage.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-collection?u=76281980&t=5)** The more prepared we are for issues that might crop up, the more likely we'll identify and resolve them.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-collection?u=76281980&t=10)** So let's get into it.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-collection?u=76281980&t=11)** The biggest challenge we'll face when collecting data is the data quality.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-collection?u=76281980&t=16)** It's been a common theme so far, so you already know how important this is.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-collection?u=76281980&t=21)** Data collection can really be hampered by inaccurate data entry, duplicate records, or incomplete records.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-collection?u=76281980&t=27)** All of this can challenge the quality of our entire process.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-collection?u=76281980&t=31)** Luckily, we've already covered some ways to mitigate this with data validation and ways to identify duplicates.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-collection?u=76281980&t=38)** Another challenge is the sheer quantity of diverse data sources.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-collection?u=76281980&t=42)** Collecting data from many sources in many formats and bringing it into a process where it can all be used for one goal is not easy.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-collection?u=76281980&t=50)** You'll also probably find the existence of data silos, where some systems are completely isolated from others, making it hard to bring data together from different sources to create one complete useful picture.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-collection?u=76281980&t=62)** There are also technical challenges.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-collection?u=76281980&t=64)** These could be due to a lack of required tools or skills to get the job done in the first place, or it could be related to scale.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-collection?u=76281980&t=72)** Are data collection techniques in place able to meet the demand of increased volumes of data within an acceptable timeframe?
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-collection?u=76281980&t=80)** It's also really important to consider security.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-collection?u=76281980&t=82)** I have a whole chapter coming up on governance and data security, but it's worth highlighting now that there is a responsibility as we collect data to keep it safe.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-collection?u=76281980&t=91)** The risk of data breach in today's world is very real, so we need to ensure that we are using secure collection and transmission procedures to minimize these risks.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-collection?u=76281980&t=101)** Data management is often thought of as a technical problem, something we will implement using tools and techniques, but it also involves people.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-collection?u=76281980&t=109)** One of the challenges can be getting the people you need on board with this endeavor.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-collection?u=76281980&t=113)** People can cause a real challenge if they're not invested or they don't have the time to contribute to the project.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-collection?u=76281980&t=119)** As you can see, this isn't an easy stage of the process.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-collection?u=76281980&t=123)** In fact, spoiler alert, none of this is easy, but I like to think that by highlighting some of the challenges for each phase of this lifecycle, we'll be more equipped to plan and deal with any challenges that crop up.

#### Ethics with data collection
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/ethics-with-data-collection?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/ethics-with-data-collection?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] As mentioned in our best practice video, there needs to be a real consideration into ethics when we talk about data collection.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/ethics-with-data-collection?u=76281980&t=6)** This is becoming a really important subject, so I wanted to make sure we cover this in some detail here in this final video for this chapter.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/ethics-with-data-collection?u=76281980&t=14)** Ethical data collection is all about ensuring we respect the privacy, rights, and consent of all individuals for whom we are collecting data.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/ethics-with-data-collection?u=76281980&t=21)** It also takes into consideration that we are meeting regulatory requirements.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/ethics-with-data-collection?u=76281980&t=27)** In my mind, one of the first things we should think about is transparency, meaning that our customers know what data we are collecting about them and their activities and what we're going to do with that data.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/ethics-with-data-collection?u=76281980&t=37)** Being transparent means our customers understand exactly what is happening and that there is no deception, and if they aren't happy, they can easily do something about it.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/ethics-with-data-collection?u=76281980&t=45)** Perhaps by opting out of certain data collection practices.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/ethics-with-data-collection?u=76281980&t=50)** Data privacy is also an important topic.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/ethics-with-data-collection?u=76281980&t=52)** Some of the data we collect could be sensitive, or personally identifiable, PII and needs to be handled in appropriate ways.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/ethics-with-data-collection?u=76281980&t=60)** In some cases, we could use data aggregation, or anonymization to remove the personal details from our dataset without losing the ability to provide the needed analysis.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/ethics-with-data-collection?u=76281980&t=70)** There are also regulations such as GDPR that specify allowed data retention periods.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/ethics-with-data-collection?u=76281980&t=76)** Complying with these means that we balance our wish for data with the needs and requests of our customers.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/ethics-with-data-collection?u=76281980&t=82)** Other regulations, such as the right to be forgotten also need to be addressed.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/ethics-with-data-collection?u=76281980&t=87)** If a customer requests their data is removed from our systems, we must be able to complete that request.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/ethics-with-data-collection?u=76281980&t=94)** One final thought, when we're collecting data.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/ethics-with-data-collection?u=76281980&t=97)** We have already talked extensively about the importance of having accurate data, the ethical piece here is to avoid any collection bias.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/ethics-with-data-collection?u=76281980&t=104)** It's very important that we ensure we collect data in a way that is both fair and avoids discrimination.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/ethics-with-data-collection?u=76281980&t=111)** At the end of the day, when I'm thinking about ethical data practices for data collection, I think about my own data that's out there and how I would expect other companies to collect and treat my personal data.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/ethics-with-data-collection?u=76281980&t=122)** If you don't feel right about something happening to your personal data, your customers probably don't feel great about it either.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/ethics-with-data-collection?u=76281980&t=128)** Alright, that wraps up the chapter on data collection.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/ethics-with-data-collection?u=76281980&t=131)** Now that we have our data, it's time to move on to the next stage of the lifecycle, which is data processing and integration.

#### Data cleaning and preprocessing
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-cleaning-and-preprocessing?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-cleaning-and-preprocessing?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] The first topic we're going to discuss when it comes to data processing is Data Cleaning.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-cleaning-and-preprocessing?u=76281980&t=4)** We've probably all heard the phrase, "Garbage in, garbage out", and that is the opposite of what we're aiming for here.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-cleaning-and-preprocessing?u=76281980&t=11)** As we've already learned, this data is going to be used to make business decisions, and we don't want those to be based on garbage data.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-cleaning-and-preprocessing?u=76281980&t=18)** As soon as we get our hands on data, we want to think about improving the quality of it.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-cleaning-and-preprocessing?u=76281980&t=22)** There are three common data quality issues we want to avoid, missing data, duplicate data, and inconsistent data.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-cleaning-and-preprocessing?u=76281980&t=30)** In the previous chapter, we did touch on duplicate data, and how that can negatively impact our results.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-cleaning-and-preprocessing?u=76281980&t=36)** And remember, we can use some techniques to find and remove those duplicates, which will clean up our data and improve the quality.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-cleaning-and-preprocessing?u=76281980&t=44)** For missing data, we can also apply some techniques to help.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-cleaning-and-preprocessing?u=76281980&t=47)** This could be filling in missing values with averages or calculated estimates.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-cleaning-and-preprocessing?u=76281980&t=52)** The maths will depend on the kind of data that you're cleaning, but if you do have missing values, try to think about that data dataset as a whole, and based on the values you do have, what makes sense for each situation?
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-cleaning-and-preprocessing?u=76281980&t=63)** Identifying and rectifying inconsistent data is also not an easy task.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-cleaning-and-preprocessing?u=76281980&t=68)** Again, depending on the type of data we're cleaning, we can look at the overall dataset and highlight outliers and potential issues within the dataset, before diving into those specific values and determining whether they should be kept.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-cleaning-and-preprocessing?u=76281980&t=81)** It's possible if you're finding a lot of data quality issues at this stage, that you might want to revisit some of the previous stages of the lifecycle, such as data collection, and ensure that as much as possible is being done to collect high-quality data from the source.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-cleaning-and-preprocessing?u=76281980&t=95)** It's often a lot easier to rectify problems upstream than it is to constantly try to clean data up.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-cleaning-and-preprocessing?u=76281980&t=101)** There are a lot of tools that can be used to help with this step.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-cleaning-and-preprocessing?u=76281980&t=104)** They can start as basic a spreadsheet software, such as Microsoft Excel, where you can add calculations such as averages to missing data, or perhaps create pivot tables to help summarize and review the dataset as a whole.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-cleaning-and-preprocessing?u=76281980&t=118)** However, as our data management strategy matures, we're probably going to want to move on from Excel, to something like Python, and specifically the Pandas Library, which is an open-source library that can assist with all sorts of data cleaning, transformations and analysis.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-cleaning-and-preprocessing?u=76281980&t=133)** As well as just cleaning our data to remove any issues, we might also want to apply some pre-processing steps.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-cleaning-and-preprocessing?u=76281980&t=140)** This could be to smooth data out and reduce noise, or to remove some of the variables included to improve efficiency.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-cleaning-and-preprocessing?u=76281980&t=148)** These techniques can help to ensure we have the best possible data for the next steps in our lifecycle.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-cleaning-and-preprocessing?u=76281980&t=153)** There'll be no garbage in, garbage out in our strategies.

#### Data transformation techniques
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] All right, our data is looking better after the last video where we talked about cleaning it up.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=4)** Next, I want to think about how we can transform my data from the current raw format into more structured and usable formats.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=12)** This is where keeping that end goal in mind is really important.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=15)** What is a usable format?
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=18)** This depends on how we want to use that data in the final stages of this lifecycle where I'm creating reports and making decisions.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=25)** Let's think about aggregation to start with.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=28)** The concept of aggregation is pretty straightforward.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=30)** It's just rolling up data into categories or groups that create summaries.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=35)** For example, the raw data coming from our point of sale terminals, it's going to be individual sales.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=41)** Each sale that is made by a customer is recorded, but do I need to keep that granularity of data for my end goals?
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=48)** This isn't an easy question.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=49)** This depends entirely on what the end goal is.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=53)** If we decide that what we really care about isn't how much each individual sale is, but how much I sell per day, we can instead aggregate this data by date.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=62)** Just like that, my data has been transformed.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=65)** Aggregation is a common transformation technique, but we could also make the data more useful by thinking about data types.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=73)** Storing data in the correct data type will make things a lot easier in the long run.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=79)** Let's look at the dates in our sales data.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=82)** If we store that as a string or text value, things could get confusing.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=86)** Is that first date in May or in August?
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=89)** The currency is great British pounds, and in the U.K. dates are usually formatted day, month, year.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=95)** Whereas in the USA it's month, day, year.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=99)** Storing this data as a datetime will ensure that when we bring data together, we are comparing like-for-like.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=106)** Also with currencies, maybe we transform the sales from our multinational company all into U.S. dollars before we continue on into the analysis phase.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=115)** This allows comparisons to be made more easily.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=119)** One final transformational technique I want to mention is labeling or categorizing data.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=125)** As already discussed, the volume of data that comes through this process could be massive and sometimes overwhelming.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=131)** Providing some categories to data in this stage can help create a lot of value later on.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=136)** For example, with unstructured data like customer reviews, you could label them as positive or negative, which would provide value when you came to look at overall satisfaction based on location or the store they visited.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=150)** These transformational techniques are really important as we process our data to get it ready for use.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-transformation-techniques?u=76281980&t=155)** Let's now take a look at how this fits into an ETL process.
