#### Extract, transform, load (ETL) processes
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Alright, let's talk about ETL processes.
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=3)** ETL stands for Extract, Transform, and Load, and is a particular data integration process used for data warehousing.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=12)** In the previous video I talked about general data transformation.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=16)** ETL differs from this because of its very structured approach from moving data from various sources into one centralized data warehouse.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=25)** Whereas general data transformation is more about individual steps such as standardizing or aggregating data.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=34)** The first step of the process is extracting the data from the source system.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=38)** This could be multiple sources such as databases, APIs, or files.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=44)** The data at this point is extremely raw and can also be in multiple formats, which can add complexities to the process.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=52)** Another potential challenge to keep in mind for this step, if you're using real time data sources, there could be latency involved and then being kept up to date that will delay when you can start the extraction process.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=65)** Also, if you have a large amount of data in your source system, you might want to look into a technique called change data capture, or CDC, where you keep track of what has been updated, so only changes from the source system need to be extracted during this process.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=82)** Once the data has been extracted, it must be transformed into usable content.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=87)** Data is cleaned and processed into a standard format and type that fits the requirements of the destination system.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=96)** The techniques discussed in the previous video can be used here.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=99)** For example, standardizing currency.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=102)** So all sales are stored in USD instead of local currencies.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=108)** Throughout this stage, you should consider the data lineage.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=111)** This is basically documentation of the journey data has taken through the process.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=117)** It's important to keep track of where data has come from and how it's been transformed.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=122)** This can help when troubleshooting or providing information for audits.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=127)** Once the data is in the required format and structured in a way that makes sense, it will then be loaded into the data warehouse.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=134)** Data can be loaded either in bulk or in an incremental fashion.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=139)** These ETL processes are often pretty sizable and can take a long time to run.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=145)** When designing this phase of the system, it's important to take into account whether past data will have changed and should be reloaded, and also the volume of data.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=155)** Is it realistic to reload all the data?
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=159)** It is likely that this process will run on a schedule, probably nightly, to reprocess new data and update the data warehouse ready for reporting.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=169)** These ETL processes are often pretty sizable and can take a long time to run.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=174)** You need to keep an eye on the total processing time and look for optimizations to ensure can meet the required SLAs or service level agreements.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=183)** You should also consider recovery mechanisms.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=186)** If the ETL process fails, are there options to restart from the failure or do you need to restart the whole process?
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/etl-extract-transform-load-processes?u=76281980&t=194)** Thinking about this as you design the process can save a lot of headaches later on.

#### Data integration approaches
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-integration-approaches?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-integration-approaches?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Next up, data integration, another massive step in our data processing stage.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-integration-approaches?u=76281980&t=7)** Data integration is the process of combining data sources into a unified view.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-integration-approaches?u=76281980&t=13)** As we work through this processing stage, we are focusing on the end goal of creating a data set that will inspire great business decisions.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-integration-approaches?u=76281980&t=23)** These decisions aren't going to be made by looking at silos of data.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-integration-approaches?u=76281980&t=27)** Instead, we want that single pane of glass that will show me the whole picture.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-integration-approaches?u=76281980&t=33)** There are several methods for data integration, ranging from manual all the way up to automated.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-integration-approaches?u=76281980&t=39)** Manual integration requires data engineers to set up connections and move data around to create the required view into the data.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-integration-approaches?u=76281980&t=49)** On the other hand, automated integration will be something like the ETL processing that you read about in the last segment.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-integration-approaches?u=76281980&t=56)** We can extract data from many disparate sources and then transform them into this single data set.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-integration-approaches?u=76281980&t=63)** There are many options between manual and fully automated integration, each with their own pros and cons.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-integration-approaches?u=76281980&t=70)** But as our data management strategy matures, we are going to want to be aiming to be as automated as possible.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-integration-approaches?u=76281980&t=78)** Think again about my sales data.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-integration-approaches?u=76281980&t=80)** Looking at this, I can see that Janet is a repeat customer.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-integration-approaches?u=76281980&t=84)** She comes most days.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-integration-approaches?u=76281980&t=86)** But Bob and Stephanie have only come once.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-integration-approaches?u=76281980&t=89)** Yes, this is a small dataset, but imagine this on a bigger scale.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-integration-approaches?u=76281980&t=95)** Why did Bob not come back?
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-integration-approaches?u=76281980&t=97)** If I can integrate some nonstructured data into this data set, I can see that both Bob and Stephanie went to a certain store and had a really bad experience.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-integration-approaches?u=76281980&t=108)** This could highlight a pattern that tells us we have a store that's underperforming because they aren't getting repeat customers.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-integration-approaches?u=76281980&t=115)** This kind of data integration can provide reasons for the way data looks, which is exactly what we want at the end of this process.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-integration-approaches?u=76281980&t=124)** The aim is to create a holistic view of our data which allows us to really understand what's happening and what's affecting metrics such as sales and revenue.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-integration-approaches?u=76281980&t=134)** Understanding why structured sales data looks a particular way allows us to take actionable steps to improve.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-integration-approaches?u=76281980&t=142)** We should also consider whether this data integration needs to happen as part of a batch process or in a more real-time fashion.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-integration-approaches?u=76281980&t=150)** For our example above, the integration is probably most suited to batch processing.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-integration-approaches?u=76281980&t=155)** Perhaps the nightly ETL job pools these sources together, and we can see the results the next day.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-integration-approaches?u=76281980&t=162)** However, think about more time-sensitive data.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-integration-approaches?u=76281980&t=166)** For example, if we're working on fraud detection, seconds matter here, so real-time integration of data sources is vital.

>

#### Real-time data processing
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/real-time-data-processing?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/real-time-data-processing?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] There are two types of data processing that I think deserve a special mention.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/real-time-data-processing?u=76281980&t=4)** The first is real-time data processing.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/real-time-data-processing?u=76281980&t=6)** Data that is real time and streamed can provide useful insights to our data management strategy but needs to be handled in a totally different fashion than a more traditional batch data source.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/real-time-data-processing?u=76281980&t=18)** IoT devices, which stands for Internet of Things, for example, can stream metrics directly from the manufacturing floor, reporting on how machines are working, perhaps using temperatures and vibration metrics that help determine when machines might fail.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/real-time-data-processing?u=76281980&t=32)** It's also becoming more of a focus for companies to be energy efficient.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/real-time-data-processing?u=76281980&t=36)** IoT sensors can be used to track energy usage across the plant and help to highlight areas where savings could be made.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/real-time-data-processing?u=76281980&t=44)** Apart from IoT devices though, there could also be real-time data from financial transactions.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/real-time-data-processing?u=76281980&t=50)** This data, if handled and processed in a real-time fashion, can help to identify fraud as it's happening, and that credit card could be blocked, saving the company money.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/real-time-data-processing?u=76281980&t=60)** Real-time data processing is all about getting the data from the source to the decision- maker as quickly as possible.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/real-time-data-processing?u=76281980&t=66)** Being able to make decisions in a fast and accurate manner can allow the company to be agile and quick to respond in situations.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/real-time-data-processing?u=76281980&t=73)** This real-time data can also be integrated with more traditional sources that I've already mentioned.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/real-time-data-processing?u=76281980&t=79)** As you look around your organization and highlight real-time data that could be useful, think about the volume of data that could be generated.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/real-time-data-processing?u=76281980&t=87)** Often in these scenarios, data points are coming thick and fast, so it's important to focus on collecting only what you need, aggregating where possible, and designing your processes to handle the potential scale.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/real-time-data-processing?u=76281980&t=99)** The second special data use case I want to mention is big data, and I'll talk about that in the next video.

#### Big data processing
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/big-data-processing?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/big-data-processing?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] Big data has become a buzzword in organizations over the last few years, and it comes with a different set of challenges than more traditional data sources.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/big-data-processing?u=76281980&t=8)** But first, what even is big data in the data world?
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/big-data-processing?u=76281980&t=12)** Big data is often defined by the three Vs.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/big-data-processing?u=76281980&t=14)** Volume, velocity, and variety.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/big-data-processing?u=76281980&t=17)** Volume is the sheer amount of the data.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/big-data-processing?u=76281980&t=21)** This is often measured in terabytes, petabytes, or even exabytes.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/big-data-processing?u=76281980&t=25)** As more and more devices are connected to the internet, it's becoming easier to create huge amounts of data.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/big-data-processing?u=76281980&t=31)** The second V is velocity, and this is the speed in which data is created, processed and used.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/big-data-processing?u=76281980&t=37)** Think about the stock exchange and how many transactions and price changes happen in every second.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/big-data-processing?u=76281980&t=44)** The third V is variety.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/big-data-processing?u=76281980&t=46)** The data doesn't always have to be the same type.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/big-data-processing?u=76281980&t=49)** Some could be structured, some could be unstructured, but this combination can bring challenges, but also deep insights.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/big-data-processing?u=76281980&t=57)** Now that we know what big data is, it's easier to see some of the challenges we might face as we try and process this data into something that can create meaningful insights.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/big-data-processing?u=76281980&t=67)** Scalability is, again, worth mentioning.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/big-data-processing?u=76281980&t=69)** We talked about the volume of data here.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/big-data-processing?u=76281980&t=71)** We've got to have systems and storage in place that can handle this amount of data and be able to process it in a timely manner.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/big-data-processing?u=76281980&t=79)** Although this isn't the same as real-time data where we want to make decisions as close to the time the data was generated as possible, we still want to make decisions in a timely fashion.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/big-data-processing?u=76281980&t=89)** It will be no good if it took days to process this data.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/big-data-processing?u=76281980&t=92)** By the time it was ready to be used to make decisions, it will be out of date and no longer valuable.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/big-data-processing?u=76281980&t=98)** Big data is used in all kinds of industries, healthcare, finance, retail, and many more.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/big-data-processing?u=76281980&t=105)** Over the last couple of years, there have been a number of case studies where big data has helped to improve the early detection and treatment of cancer.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/big-data-processing?u=76281980&t=112)** The vast amount of data that has been collected, processed and analyzed has been able to provide insights that on smaller data sets wouldn't have been apparent.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/big-data-processing?u=76281980&t=120)** That's a pretty powerful use case.

#### Challenges in data processing and integration
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-processing-and-integration?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-processing-and-integration?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] This data processing stage of our lifecycle is vital for getting high quality, complete, consistent, and useful data to our decision makers.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-processing-and-integration?u=76281980&t=8)** However, none of this is easy.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-processing-and-integration?u=76281980&t=9)** I want to highlight a few of the challenges you might face in this stage and provide some ideas for conquering them.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-processing-and-integration?u=76281980&t=16)** Data quality issues are the biggest challenge here.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-processing-and-integration?u=76281980&t=18)** As we integrate data from multiple sources in many different formats, it's likely there will be inconsistencies or missing data.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-processing-and-integration?u=76281980&t=26)** Making sure to prioritize the data cleaning I've talked about in this chapter will help to mitigate these challenges and leave you on a strong foot for the next stage.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-processing-and-integration?u=76281980&t=35)** Probably the second biggest challenge is being able to scale as more data sources are integrated, or as the business grows, the amount of data that is going to flow through the system is going to increase.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-processing-and-integration?u=76281980&t=46)** Designing a system that has the ability to scale and manage these increases and still performs is vital to our project being a success.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-processing-and-integration?u=76281980&t=54)** Throughout all the decisions you make in this process, it's important to think about the future and whether this choice would scale Hand in hand with the ability to scale is the resource cost that is involved in the process.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-processing-and-integration?u=76281980&t=67)** It's important to balance the amount of data, the process, the efficiency of the process, and the cost involved.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-processing-and-integration?u=76281980&t=73)** These three considerations need to be discussed with every decision that is made to ensure the best possible outcome.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-processing-and-integration?u=76281980&t=81)** Another challenge is when humans are involved in the process.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-processing-and-integration?u=76281980&t=84)** If there are steps that require manual intervention by humans, there is always the possibility for mistakes.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-processing-and-integration?u=76281980&t=90)** It's important to try and automate as many of these tasks as possible.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-processing-and-integration?u=76281980&t=96)** There are some mitigation strategies, though we have a chapter coming up later in the course dedicated to data governance.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-processing-and-integration?u=76281980&t=102)** Data governance is one way that we can try and avoid these pitfalls using frameworks to ensure data quality and security throughout the whole process.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-processing-and-integration?u=76281980&t=111)** As you can see, the stage isn't easy, but it's vital.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/challenges-in-data-processing-and-integration?u=76281980&t=114)** So spend a good amount of time discussing these options available to clean and process the incoming data into the best possible end product.

#### Practical look at pipelines
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Pipelines can be used throughout your data processing to move data around and transform it from raw data into beautifully curated datasets to report off of.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=10)** There are many options for pipelines too, depending on the tools available to you and where your data is.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=18)** I'm going to show you one option to get more of a grasp of how we can use a data pipeline within Fabric to import data from a CSV file in blob storage into our data warehouse.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=30)** Microsoft Fabric is an end-to-end analytics platform.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=34)** It does everything you might need when thinking about data analytics.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=38)** If you want to learn more, there are several Fabric courses in the LinkedIn Learning Library.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=44)** The concepts here are specific to Fabric, but we'll transfer to most other pipeline technologies.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=52)** So in the Azure portal, you can see I have a storage account called stlinkedindata002, which has a container called eventdata2.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=63)** And in there is a CSV file called, new_york_events_2010_2015.csv.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=70)** We need to integrate this into our sample New York City taxi cab data that we have in our data warehouse.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=79)** Let me switch over to Fabric and open up the PL-LinkedIn-EventData pipeline, and let's take a look at how this works.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=91)** This pipeline is pretty simple.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=93)** I've got a copy data task, a script, and then depending on whether the script was successful, either a success or a failure email will be sent.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=103)** Let's take a look at each step to see what's happening.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=109)** Step one is the copy data step.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=111)** And if we look at the source, we can see it has a connection to blob storage, to the eventdata2 container, and the CSV file we saw at the beginning of this video.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=121)** It's configured to be a delimited text file.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=124)** And in settings for that, you can see the column delimiter is a comma.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=133)** On the Destination tab, you can see the connection to the data warehouse, and I've selected Auto-create table.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=140)** So if the table isn't found, the pipeline will automatically create it for us.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=145)** I've left the rest of the options as the defaults for now.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=151)** The second step is a script task to write a log message.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=155)** You can see on the Settings tab, it has a connection to the data warehouse, and then an insert statement to log the time and that the pipeline executed.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=167)** Then, depending on whether the script task was successful or not, an email is sent.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=172)** You can see an email address, subject, and body, which can contain dynamic content, like the ID of our pipeline or output from any of the other tasks.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=183)** You'll notice that these steps are deactivated in my pipeline, so they won't run.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=187)** This task is still in preview at the moment, and the connections aren't enabled for my Office 365 account, so the tasks fail.
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=195)** But Fabric development is moving fast, it's likely that by the time you're watching this course that those tasks and many more are available.
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=207)** Anyway, let's execute this pipeline by pressing Run, and we'll see the execution progress in the Output section.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=228)** You can see that the tasks were successful, and some runtime stats are provided such as durations.
>
> **[4:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=252)** Let's pop back into the data warehouse and refresh the table nodes.
>
> **[4:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=256)** You can see we now have an events table.
>
> **[4:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=259)** If I run a Select TOP 100, you can see the data has been loaded.
>
> **[4:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=273)** And finally, reviewing the log table shows my pipeline has executed.
>
> **[4:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-pipelines?u=76281980&t=279)** As I mentioned, this is just a simple pipeline, but it's a really powerful tool for moving data around and applying transformations.

>

>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-storage?u=76281980&t=43)** However, we still need to optimize the storage we're using and make sure that we choose the right option for the data we want to store.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-storage?u=76281980&t=51)** I'll covered data archiving, this is not just important for keeping costs down.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-storage?u=76281980&t=55)** We don't want to store data we don't need, but it's also important for regulatory reasons.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-storage?u=76281980&t=60)** Retention periods should be in place for certain types of data to ensure we're not keeping more data than we are allowed to.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-storage?u=76281980&t=67)** I'll also touch on backups since I started my IT career as a database administrator, ensuring the data is backed up is high on my priority list, and depending on how we're storing data, the backup requirements change.

#### Types of data storage
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-storage?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-storage?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] As you've come to expect from this course so far, we have decisions to make in this chapter.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-storage?u=76281980&t=5)** We've already discussed that there is a vast number of data sources that we can pull data from, in a vast number of formats, so as you can imagine, we have a lot of storage options available too.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-storage?u=76281980&t=15)** I'm going to introduce five data storage options we have available to us, and we'll dive into more details in the following videos.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-storage?u=76281980&t=21)** It's important to have a good overview of the options before we start, to focus on which one we want to choose.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-storage?u=76281980&t=28)** Number one is relational databases.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-storage?u=76281980&t=31)** These are perfect for storing structured data that is organized into tables with rows and columns.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-storage?u=76281980&t=37)** If our data is semi-structured or unstructured, we could instead consider option two, which is NoSQL databases.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-storage?u=76281980&t=44)** NoSQL databases provide more flexibility when handling this less structured data.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-storage?u=76281980&t=51)** Number three is data warehouses.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-storage?u=76281980&t=52)** These are centralized repositories that are optimized for analytics and reporting.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-storage?u=76281980&t=57)** We'll likely want to end up with one of these as the basis for our reporting system to enable our business users to make their decisions.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-storage?u=76281980&t=65)** We might also base our reporting systems directly off of option number four, which is a data lake.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-storage?u=76281980&t=71)** Data lakes are great for storing vast quantities of unstructured or semi-structured data in native formats.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-storage?u=76281980&t=78)** Finally, option five has become more prevalent in recent years, and that is cloud storage.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-storage?u=76281980&t=83)** This offers easily scalable, cost-effective options for storing data.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-storage?u=76281980&t=89)** Cloud storage is really interesting, because we have some options that are only available in the cloud, such as AWS S3 buckets or Azure Blob storage, but we also have some options that are available on premises and in the cloud, such as Microsoft SQL Server.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-storage?u=76281980&t=104)** Let's investigate some of these options in more detail, and you'll be in the position to make well-informed decisions about which data storage option to use for each scenario.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-storage?u=76281980&t=113)** It's also important to realize there isn't one right answer here.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/types-of-data-storage?u=76281980&t=116)** It's possible that our overall data management strategy will include a hybrid approach with data stored in different storage options.

#### Database management systems (DBMS)
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/database-management-systems-dbms?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/database-management-systems-dbms?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] Now, as I mentioned, I started my IT career as a database administrator, so obviously, my favorite storage option is a database management system or DBMS, but it's not always the right option.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/database-management-systems-dbms?u=76281980&t=11)** Let's talk about what a DBMS is and when it's the right option for storing the data.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/database-management-systems-dbms?u=76281980&t=17)** There are two main flavors of DBMS, relational and non-relational.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/database-management-systems-dbms?u=76281980&t=21)** Depending on the type of data we have will determine which is the best option for our use case.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/database-management-systems-dbms?u=76281980&t=26)** Some examples of relational databases are Microsoft SQL Server, Oracle, or MySQL.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/database-management-systems-dbms?u=76281980&t=32)** There are differences between these systems, such as licensing requirements, price points, and features, but they're all good at storing structured data in tables with columns and rows.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/database-management-systems-dbms?u=76281980&t=43)** On the other hand, non-relational databases are good for storing semi-structured or unstructured data.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/database-management-systems-dbms?u=76281980&t=49)** These databases can be further broken up into the kind of data they store.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/database-management-systems-dbms?u=76281980&t=55)** Some examples will be document databases such as MongoDB or CouchDB, key value stores such as Redis, which can be good for caches or session management data, or column family stores such as Apache Cassandra, which could be good for time series data.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/database-management-systems-dbms?u=76281980&t=72)** It's often wise to choose a database management system for your data when we want to centralize data.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/database-management-systems-dbms?u=76281980&t=78)** If there are multiple groups in the organization that need access, you can easily accomplish this with a database.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/database-management-systems-dbms?u=76281980&t=83)** The database system can also assist with managing security to ensure that folks can only see data that they're allowed to access.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/database-management-systems-dbms?u=76281980&t=92)** Now, this depends on the specific DBMS, but most of them are built to handle large volumes of data efficiently, and a lot of the systems come with good high availability and disaster recovery features to ensure that the data is always available to the business.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/database-management-systems-dbms?u=76281980&t=108)** These kinds of systems are often suited for transactional workloads, often called OLTP, or online transactional processing.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/database-management-systems-dbms?u=76281980&t=115)** This includes sales data or customer records, and can handle real-time processing and quick response times.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/database-management-systems-dbms?u=76281980&t=124)** Overall, using a database management system can help to provide consistent data in a safe and secure fashion across the organization.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/database-management-systems-dbms?u=76281980&t=132)** As you're thinking about the data you need to store, think about whether it's structured, semi-structured, or unstructured, and then decide whether a DBMS and which DBMS is right for your use case.

>

#### Data warehousing
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-warehousing?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-warehousing?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] In the last video, I talked about database management systems that were suited for online transactional processing or OLTP.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-warehousing?u=76281980&t=6)** The opposite of this is online analytical processing, or OLAP, which are data sets optimized for complex queries and analysis.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-warehousing?u=76281980&t=15)** OLAP data sets are stored in data warehouses, which is what this video is all about.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-warehousing?u=76281980&t=21)** Data warehouses are designed in a way where analytical queries can be run to answer questions across the data.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-warehousing?u=76281980&t=27)** They're often created as a star schema, where the central table, a fact table records specific events such as sales.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-warehousing?u=76281980&t=34)** Around the fact table are dimension tables, which describe the event, in this example, the sale.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-warehousing?u=76281980&t=40)** For example, a date dimension for when the sale took place, and a product dimension for the item that was sold, as you can see here on the Microsoft Docs page.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-warehousing?u=76281980&t=50)** This is a very different design from how data is stored in our relational databases, but is specifically for complex analytical queries that produce reports.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-warehousing?u=76281980&t=60)** Data warehouses are often created through an ETL process that we learn about in our data processing chapter.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-warehousing?u=76281980&t=65)** Data that is extracted from many sources is transformed into a shape that can be loaded into our star schema.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-warehousing?u=76281980&t=74)** Data warehouses are challenging to get right.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-warehousing?u=76281980&t=76)** There are a whole host of business questions that need to be thoroughly thought through to achieve the results we need to benefit the organization.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-warehousing?u=76281980&t=83)** For example, when we think about sales data, what dimensions do we want to be able to report off of?
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-warehousing?u=76281980&t=89)** Do we care about the store the sale happened in?
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-warehousing?u=76281980&t=91)** If yes, we need to include a dimension with store information.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-warehousing?u=76281980&t=96)** If sales happen across the globe, maybe we need a region or a country dimension to enable reporting for those scenarios.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-warehousing?u=76281980&t=104)** As you can imagine, these models can get complex fast, and this is often where the challenges arise.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-warehousing?u=76281980&t=110)** Also, remember, the more dimensions we want to store, the more data we are storing.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-warehousing?u=76281980&t=115)** This will increase resource costs to store and process all that data.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-warehousing?u=76281980&t=119)** It's important to get the right balance between granularity and complexity.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-warehousing?u=76281980&t=125)** Although this topic is hard work to get right, the results of a good data warehouse can provide great insights into the business and enable leaders to make business decisions from a reliable, solid data foundation.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-warehousing?u=76281980&t=136)** They're often a critical part of a company's overall data management strategy.

#### Data archiving and backups
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-archiving-and-backups?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-archiving-and-backups?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] So far, we've focused on collecting data, transforming into the perfect data set, and then storing it in a way that makes sense, perhaps in a relational database or a data warehouse.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-archiving-and-backups?u=76281980&t=9)** But what happens to that data as time moves on?
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-archiving-and-backups?u=76281980&t=12)** Do we just keep it forever?
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-archiving-and-backups?u=76281980&t=14)** No, we shouldn't just focus on getting the data into the system and then never removing any.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-archiving-and-backups?u=76281980&t=19)** This not only leads to growing storage costs and slower processing times, it can also create regulatory issues.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-archiving-and-backups?u=76281980&t=27)** We'll cover that aspect more in the data governance chapter, but for now, it's important to know that we have a responsibility to keep data for a certain amount of time.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-archiving-and-backups?u=76281980&t=36)** This depends on the kind of data and where in the world it's stored.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-archiving-and-backups?u=76281980&t=40)** It's really important to make sure you understand the regulations that your data needs to adhere to.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-archiving-and-backups?u=76281980&t=46)** Data archiving is an important consideration when we think about data management as a whole, and it's really difficult.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-archiving-and-backups?u=76281980&t=52)** Archiving could mean two things.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-archiving-and-backups?u=76281980&t=54)** It could mean moving data out of the current system into a cold storage solution.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-archiving-and-backups?u=76281980&t=58)** This is usually cheaper but harder to retrieve the data, or it could mean deleting data from our systems.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-archiving-and-backups?u=76281980&t=66)** What you delete will depend on retention periods.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-archiving-and-backups?u=76281980&t=68)** We'll cover what those are and how best to determine them in the next video.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-archiving-and-backups?u=76281980&t=74)** Cold storage could be a tier on your SAN that is less performant than your most expensive SSD tier, or it could be a case of moving the data into a cloud storage solution such as Azure Blob Storage or an AWS S3 Bucket.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-archiving-and-backups?u=76281980&t=88)** Another similar consideration to this topic is data backups.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-archiving-and-backups?u=76281980&t=92)** Ensuring the data that you are keeping is safe, and if something was to happen to the current system it's stored in, would you be able to recover it?
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-archiving-and-backups?u=76281980&t=101)** As with data archiving, having these conversations early can make this process a lot easier.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-archiving-and-backups?u=76281980&t=106)** Sit down and decide on the recovery point objective, RPO of each data set.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-archiving-and-backups?u=76281980&t=111)** That means if there was, say, a natural disaster that took out the data center and we had to rebuild, what's an acceptable amount of data to lose?
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-archiving-and-backups?u=76281980&t=121)** Now, a lot of people will immediately say, none.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-archiving-and-backups?u=76281980&t=123)** I can absolutely not lose any of this data.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-archiving-and-backups?u=76281980&t=126)** You can of course, design a system for this purpose, but the price tag is going to be high.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-archiving-and-backups?u=76281980&t=131)** Again, it's about finding the balance between how much money to spend and how much data you can really lose.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-archiving-and-backups?u=76281980&t=137)** Having these discussions when you know who owns the data and documenting them is a critical part of having a solid data management strategy.

#### Practical look at blob storage lifecycle management
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-blob-storage-lifecycle-management?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-blob-storage-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] In the previous video, we talked about moving data that isn't being accessed as often off of the hot fast storage onto cheaper cold storage.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-blob-storage-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=9)** We focused mostly around what that looks like on-prem, but let's take a look at how we can accomplish this in Azure with lifecycle management.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-blob-storage-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=19)** Here I am in the Azure portal and looking at my storage account.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-blob-storage-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=24)** This is the overview page, and you can see general information about performance, replication, and some service-specific settings.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-blob-storage-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=35)** On the left, under data management, there is a page for lifecycle management.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-blob-storage-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=43)** I can also easily find this by typing life into the search bar at the top of that pane.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-blob-storage-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=49)** This is something I use often as there are some resources that have a lot of pages to review.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-blob-storage-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=56)** You can see currently we don't have any rules enabled for this storage account, so let's go ahead and create our first one.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-blob-storage-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=65)** Clicking on add rule at the top will take me through to a wizard, which will guide me through the creation.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-blob-storage-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=74)** Let's add the name archive after seven days.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-blob-storage-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=78)** We'll leave the scope and the type options as the defaults.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-blob-storage-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=83)** Clicking next, I can now enter the criteria and what should happen to blobs that meet that requirement.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-blob-storage-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=91)** We'll fill in the form so if base blobs have been last modified more than seven days ago, then they should be moved to cool storage.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-blob-storage-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=102)** I'll press add to create the rule.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-blob-storage-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=106)** I'm now going to create a second rule that deletes any blobs older than 30 days.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-blob-storage-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=112)** I'll name it delete after 30 days.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-blob-storage-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=115)** Again, keep the defaults and press next.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-blob-storage-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=119)** Then I'll set the criteria to last modified more than 30 days ago, then delete the blob.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-blob-storage-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=128)** I'll again press add.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-blob-storage-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=130)** Now you can see I have two enabled rules in lifecycle management that will automatically manage the files I have in blob storage.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-blob-storage-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=138)** If a file isn't accessed within seven days, it'll be migrated to cool storage, and then if it isn't accessed within 30 days, it'll be deleted.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-blob-storage-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=155)** There are currently three options of storage you can migrate blobs to from the hot tier.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-blob-storage-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=159)** These are cool, cold, and archive.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-blob-storage-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=163)** As you move down this list, the storage gets cheaper but it's slower to access.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-blob-storage-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=168)** In the case of archive storage, you have to request the blobs be moved back from archive storage before you can access them, which can take some time.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/practical-look-at-blob-storage-lifecycle-management?u=76281980&t=178)** I hope this has provided a good visual of how migrating data between tiers can work in the cloud and consider adding some lifecycle management rules so you can automatically migrate your files and keep your storage costs down.

#### Data retention and compliance
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-retention-and-compliance?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-retention-and-compliance?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] In the previous video, we talked about archiving and backing up data.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-retention-and-compliance?u=76281980&t=4)** Both those topics depend on retention periods to know how long data should be kept.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-retention-and-compliance?u=76281980&t=9)** As you're collecting data and planning out the storage of your data, you should already be thinking about setting retention periods for that data.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-retention-and-compliance?u=76281980&t=16)** Some retention periods will be mandated by regulations such as GDPR or financial data requirements, but I cannot stress the importance of documenting how long data should be kept at the beginning of this process.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-retention-and-compliance?u=76281980&t=28)** I have had many conversations with businesses where they have had way more data than they need years and years of data that is barely useful at this point, but when you ask about retention periods, no one knows who owns that data and who should be the one to make that decision.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-retention-and-compliance?u=76281980&t=43)** If you can get that decision in writing by the folks requesting or collecting this data in the first place, it makes it a much easier in the long run.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-retention-and-compliance?u=76281980&t=52)** For example, under GDPR, personal information and performance reviews about your employees can only be retained for six years after employment ends.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-retention-and-compliance?u=76281980&t=61)** This means you need to track employment dates for anyone you employ, and then have a cleanup strategy based on that.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-retention-and-compliance?u=76281980&t=69)** GDPR also requires that financial and transactional records are kept for at least six years to comply with tax and legal requirements.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-retention-and-compliance?u=76281980&t=76)** Perhaps you don't need all six years online in your OLTP database though, so you could use a guideline to develop an archiving strategy where financial data is kept in the database for three years to allow for easy reporting, but then is archived into secure flat files that are kept in cheaper storage.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-retention-and-compliance?u=76281980&t=94)** Keeping track of these regulations is hard work.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-retention-and-compliance?u=76281980&t=96)** As you're working through your data management strategy, I would recommend that you document what types of data you have where, and what the retention periods of it should be.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-retention-and-compliance?u=76281980&t=106)** These retention periods don't necessarily have to be forced by GDPR.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-retention-and-compliance?u=76281980&t=110)** Perhaps you only really care about the last three years of detailed customer sales data, so after that date, you could decide to roll it up and only store it as aggregated data.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-retention-and-compliance?u=76281980&t=120)** This kind of retention period is determined and managed by your organization and the stakeholders.

#### Data storage optimization
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-storage-optimization?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-storage-optimization?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] As we're storing more and more data, we need to think about how to optimize this storage so that we can keep our resource costs down and our efficiency up.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-storage-optimization?u=76281980&t=8)** When we talked about archiving, we talked about moving data to cold storage, but what does this really mean?
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-storage-optimization?u=76281980&t=14)** Well, it depends, of course.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-storage-optimization?u=76281980&t=16)** If you have an on-premises data center, then you probably have some kind of San storage area network that helps to provide reliable, fast storage to multiple servers.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-storage-optimization?u=76281980&t=25)** It's possible that this sand contains multiple tiers of storage.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-storage-optimization?u=76281980&t=29)** The data you access often will be on your hot tier, which will be your fastest storage, probably flash.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-storage-optimization?u=76281980&t=35)** Then data that is accessed less can be relegated onto warm or cold tiers.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-storage-optimization?u=76281980&t=40)** As you can imagine, the hot tier with flash storage is more expensive, so you only want to store mission critical data there.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-storage-optimization?u=76281980&t=47)** For example, just the last day's data for certain applications.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-storage-optimization?u=76281980&t=51)** As time goes on, people will access that data less so it can be moved off of the hot, expensive tier onto a cheaper storage tier.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-storage-optimization?u=76281980&t=59)** Quite often this can happen automatically.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-storage-optimization?u=76281980&t=61)** The sand technology will take care of migrating that data.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-storage-optimization?u=76281980&t=66)** Another technique to save money and storage space is to use deduplication techniques.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-storage-optimization?u=76281980&t=71)** This is where blocks that are the same are only stored once.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-storage-optimization?u=76281980&t=74)** Large data sets often have a lot of duplicate data, so this can greatly reduce the required storage footprint.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-storage-optimization?u=76281980&t=82)** This is a feature that can cause quite a lot of discussion between storage admins and application admins.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-storage-optimization?u=76281980&t=87)** There are times where deduplication can cause overhead, so serving data takes a little longer, and then that is felt in the application with slower response times.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-storage-optimization?u=76281980&t=96)** As with all things, it's best to get a performance baseline and test this out before enabling it in production.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-storage-optimization?u=76281980&t=103)** So far, these concepts have been focused on premises, but there are similar options in the cloud.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-storage-optimization?u=76281980&t=109)** For example, not all of our cloud storage options are at the same price point, so it is possible to archive data out of our mission critical SQL server and store those files, perhaps backups in blob storage.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-storage-optimization?u=76281980&t=121)** If we need to get the data back, it'll take a little time and effort, but it'll save a lot of money and potentially keep performance high by not keeping it in the active database.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-storage-optimization?u=76281980&t=131)** We have a lot of options available when we think about storing data and technologies like tiered sands, data deduplication and cheaper cloud storage options can help us keep our resource costs under control.

### 5. Data Analysis and Interpretation

> [[#Table of Contents|↑ Back to Table of Contents]]

#### Introduction to data analysis
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-analysis?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=0)** - Welcome to the next stage of our data management lifecycle.
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=3)** We've made it to data analysis.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=5)** This is where we extract useful information from the data we've collected, processed, and stored in the previous stages.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=11)** Remembering our end goal is to provide data that can drive business decisions, we have to find the insights within the data we have available to us.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=20)** In this chapter, we'll walk through several techniques that can be used to help find these insights, including exploratory data analysis or EDA, where we start to identify patterns and understand the data structures.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=32)** We'll also talk about predictive analysis and modeling where we analyze the current data we have and use it to forecast or make predictions of what might happen next.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=42)** These data sets could be large, which makes some of this analysis time consuming and difficult.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=46)** We'll talk about how machine learning can assist us here to apply complex algorithms to find insights previously hidden to just the human eye.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=54)** We've also talked about unstructured data in this course so far, such as customer reviews.
>

>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=65)** Once we have all these insights from our many data sources, we'll wrap up this chapter with a discussion on how best to interpret and communicate these results.

> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=72)** It's going to be an insightful chapter.
