#### Exploratory data analysis (EDA)
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/exploratory-data-analysis-eda?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/exploratory-data-analysis-eda?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] The first step in this data analysis phase is really focused around understanding the data we have available to us.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/exploratory-data-analysis-eda?u=76281980&t=6)** Exploratory data analysis or EDA has exactly that goal.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/exploratory-data-analysis-eda?u=76281980&t=10)** We must understand the data structures, the attributes we have collected and how they fit together in order to create models that we can use to drive insights.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/exploratory-data-analysis-eda?u=76281980&t=20)** During this phase, we'll often uncover some initial findings, discover patterns, and detect anomalies that can help us to focus our efforts as we get further into this process.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/exploratory-data-analysis-eda?u=76281980&t=30)** Some techniques for this phase could include data visualizations such as histograms and scatterplots, which will make it easier for us to see patterns appearing from the data.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/exploratory-data-analysis-eda?u=76281980&t=40)** For example, if we plot sales against the month of the year, we could see clear patterns developing, which would help us to determine if our sales are affected by the seasons.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/exploratory-data-analysis-eda?u=76281980&t=49)** Depending on what we decided in the earlier stages, we may have integrated third party data into our models, such as weather reports.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/exploratory-data-analysis-eda?u=76281980&t=56)** In this case, we could also plot sales against weather conditions to discover whether we sell more or less on hot sunny days versus cold blustery days.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/exploratory-data-analysis-eda?u=76281980&t=65)** We've also worked hard throughout the process to ensure data quality, but it is possible that through this initial analysis we'll find anomalies that could point towards data quality concerns.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/exploratory-data-analysis-eda?u=76281980&t=75)** It's important to really think about these however, and determine if it's really a bad data point or just a strange day of high sales on a day where you would expect low sales.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/exploratory-data-analysis-eda?u=76281980&t=85)** Either way, this stage is a great time to really dig into the data, figure out what you have, what insights you can start to see, and also decide if you've collected all the data you need or want.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/exploratory-data-analysis-eda?u=76281980&t=96)** It's worth highlighting that this data management process is iterative, and so you may get to this point and realize you want to go back a stage and improve or change things.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/exploratory-data-analysis-eda?u=76281980&t=105)** Be flexible in the early days.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/exploratory-data-analysis-eda?u=76281980&t=106)** Getting this process right is hard work, so if you have to take a couple of steps back to get better results, it'll be worth it in the end.

#### Predictive analytics and modeling
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/predictive-analytics-and-modeling?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/predictive-analytics-and-modeling?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] Another technique we can use in the data analysis phase is predictive analytics and modeling.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/predictive-analytics-and-modeling?u=76281980&t=5)** The main idea here is to take the data we have collected, which tells us about what has happened in the past, and use it to create predictions for what might happen in the future.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/predictive-analytics-and-modeling?u=76281980&t=15)** This analysis relies heavily on identifying trends and patterns within the data sets, and then determining where these trends will lead.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/predictive-analytics-and-modeling?u=76281980&t=23)** If sales have steadily been increasing by a certain percent each month, you should be able to forecast sales for the months ahead, helping to ensure you have enough stock in your stores, for example.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/predictive-analytics-and-modeling?u=76281980&t=34)** There are some common techniques that can be used here, such as decision trees, regression analysis, or even by using machine learning algorithms to find patterns that are hard to identify.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/predictive-analytics-and-modeling?u=76281980&t=46)** There are some challenges though.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/predictive-analytics-and-modeling?u=76281980&t=48)** Something I have mentioned several times already is data quality.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/predictive-analytics-and-modeling?u=76281980&t=52)** If we are going to base predictions on this data, we must ensure that we have done as much as possible to ensure that quality of the data we have collected from past experience.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/predictive-analytics-and-modeling?u=76281980&t=62)** As we create models on this data that will enable these future predictions, we need to ensure the model fits the data we have.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/predictive-analytics-and-modeling?u=76281980&t=70)** Sometimes this will mean we need to create several models, test and reassess whether they really fit the data.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/predictive-analytics-and-modeling?u=76281980&t=77)** It's also important to try and keep the models from getting too complex.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/predictive-analytics-and-modeling?u=76281980&t=80)** This is a fine balance to manage these predictive models can help in many aspects of sales, as I already mentioned, such as ensuring you have the inventory available to meet demands.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/predictive-analytics-and-modeling?u=76281980&t=93)** Or as I mentioned earlier, in healthcare fields models can be used to predict disease.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/predictive-analytics-and-modeling?u=76281980&t=99)** Being able to gain insights from the past to predict the future can give your company a massive competitive advantage.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/predictive-analytics-and-modeling?u=76281980&t=105)** So it is well worth spending some time discussing how this can fit into your overall data management strategy.

#### Machine learning for data analysis
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/machine-learning-for-data-analysis?u=76281980)

>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/machine-learning-for-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] As mentioned briefly in the previous video, machine learning algorithms can help us to reveal intelligence and insights that were previously hidden to the human eye.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/machine-learning-for-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=9)** Let's dig in and see the real power and some potential uses.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/machine-learning-for-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=13)** As data volume grows, both in the amount of data we have but also in the breadth of information we have about each data point, it can become harder to find insights with techniques such as visualizations.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/machine-learning-for-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=25)** When we manually create visualizations, we need to think about which data attributes we will plot against each other.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/machine-learning-for-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=31)** For example, comparing sale with the weather on the day of the sale.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/machine-learning-for-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=36)** But as we're collecting more information around each of those sales, we would have to manually create a lot of combinations of these data points to be able to find the trends and patterns that could really drive our business forward.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/machine-learning-for-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=47)** This is where machine learning can help.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/machine-learning-for-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=51)** Machine learning, or ML, can detect patterns in large datasets by using models and algorithms.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/machine-learning-for-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=58)** The algorithms can be fed large amounts of data that you have collected, and it will help to explore and make sense of all that data.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/machine-learning-for-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=65)** The data will be broken down into features which describe the data points, and then analyzed to determine how these features interact with each other and affect things like sales.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/machine-learning-for-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=74)** This process is iterative, and as the algorithm is trained on your data, it gets smarter and smarter and is fine-tuned until it recognizes these patterns.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/machine-learning-for-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=84)** A lot of the time, the patterns that are detected by ML are not something that would've been discovered by humans looking at the same data.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/machine-learning-for-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=92)** The benefit is that computers can handle this vast amount of data and can find the insights that might be hidden within.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/machine-learning-for-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=99)** It's still worth mentioning again that data quality is key here.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/machine-learning-for-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=103)** If the algorithms are trained against data that is inaccurate, the models and therefore predictions will also not be accurate.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/machine-learning-for-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=111)** ML can be used in a wide variety of industries.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/machine-learning-for-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=114)** Similar to predictive modeling, it can be used to predict disease in the healthcare sector, or in the financial industry, it can be used to help detect fraud.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/machine-learning-for-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=123)** The potential uses of ML are huge.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/machine-learning-for-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=126)** As computers get more powerful and data scientists get smarter, these models are going to provide better and better insights, which will drive more reliable business decisions.

#### Text and sentiment analysis
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/text-and-sentiment-analysis?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/text-and-sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Some data that we collect cannot be analyzed in the same fashion that we've already discussed.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/text-and-sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=5)** Unstructured data, such as customer reviews or social media posts, for example, can't easily be plotted onto a graph to look for patterns, so how do we analyze and make use of this data?
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/text-and-sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=16)** Well, one option is text and sentiment analysis, a specific machine learning technique.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/text-and-sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=22)** Sentiment analysis is where we analyze the unstructured data, let's say social media posts about a new product, to determine if they are positive, negative, or neutral.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/text-and-sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=32)** We can't possibly read thousands or even millions of posts on social media sites, but we can use sentiment analysis to determine overall how things are looking.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/text-and-sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=42)** Sentiment analysis focuses on the words used and the context they are used in to determine whether this post is positive or not.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/text-and-sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=49)** We can then use these data points for further analysis.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/text-and-sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=53)** Combining a sentiment score with other more structured data sources can also help us to determine if there are certain demographics, for example, that are positive about our product, versus others that are providing more negative feedback.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/text-and-sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=66)** This analysis can happen quickly, and therefore can provide fast, actionable insights to the business, which can make a huge difference in the bottom line.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/text-and-sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=75)** With all machine learning, we'll need to think about continually training the models we have to ensure accuracy.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/text-and-sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=82)** For example, there are new words being used to describe positive or negative feelings all the time.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/text-and-sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=87)** If our model doesn't know these words, it will be harder for it to determine the sentiment.

> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/a-practical-look-at-azure-ai-sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=12)** Azure AI services offer many different ways of integrating AI into your applications and data management lifecycle, from natural language processing to face detection to translation services.

>

>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/a-practical-look-at-azure-ai-sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=108)** This might look like a lot of code, but you can get the sample script from the URL displayed.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/a-practical-look-at-azure-ai-sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=115)** The first time you run this, it might take a few seconds to return, and once it does, you'll see the output we've created, which displays the endpoint URL.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/a-practical-look-at-azure-ai-sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=131)** Now we need to pass our customer review as part of the JSON body to that API endpoint.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/a-practical-look-at-azure-ai-sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=137)** You can see on line 16, the text of our review.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/a-practical-look-at-azure-ai-sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=141)** Running this cell of the notebook hits the API endpoint and returns the results of the sentiment analysis.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/a-practical-look-at-azure-ai-sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=152)** This analysis is done at both the document level and for each individual sentence.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/a-practical-look-at-azure-ai-sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=158)** You can see the sentiment of the document is positive, and the confidence score for it being positive is high, meaning AI is pretty sure on this one.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/a-practical-look-at-azure-ai-sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=169)** Moving down, you can see the first sentence, "Good value for the price" was determined to be positive, again, with a high confidence score, but the second sentence was determined to be neutral, neither positive or negative, and you can see that the confidence scores explain why that rating was selected.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/a-practical-look-at-azure-ai-sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=193)** This is just a simple example of how Azure AI can perform sentiment analysis on one customer review, but you can easily integrate this into your pipelines and processes within your data management lifecycle to enhance your structured data and enable it to be used for analysis.

#### Time series analysis
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/time-series-analysis?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/time-series-analysis?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Another specific type of analysis we can perform on our data is time series analysis.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/time-series-analysis?u=76281980&t=5)** This is probably something you've seen before.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/time-series-analysis?u=76281980&t=7)** This is often used to determine patterns and trends across time.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/time-series-analysis?u=76281980&t=12)** For most businesses, the goal is to increase revenue, to grow and to become more profitable.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/time-series-analysis?u=76281980&t=17)** How do we measure and track this?
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/time-series-analysis?u=76281980&t=19)** Well, across time periods.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/time-series-analysis?u=76281980&t=22)** Plotting the data points for the metrics we care about across time can start to show whether we are meeting those goals.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/time-series-analysis?u=76281980&t=28)** Are sales increasing month over month, or year over year?
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/time-series-analysis?u=76281980&t=33)** We can also group the data into monthly averages or seasonal averages, which can help to show the patterns in our data.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/time-series-analysis?u=76281980&t=40)** Perhaps we sell ice cream, and if we look at monthly sales data, we can see it's decreasing over time.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/time-series-analysis?u=76281980&t=46)** However, ice cream sales are extremely seasonable, so we could instead group data into annual sales and compare that year over year.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/time-series-analysis?u=76281980&t=55)** Or we could just compare like months from previous years, perhaps plotting sales in June of this year compared to sales in June from the previous five years, to see how we're doing.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/time-series-analysis?u=76281980&t=67)** As you start looking at the data you have available and using some of the techniques we've reviewed in this chapter, you'll notice some of these patterns, and can therefore start to narrow down the visualizations you want to see and the patterns and insights that make sense for your organization.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/time-series-analysis?u=76281980&t=82)** With that, we've added another useful data analysis technique to our tool belt, and we can start to think about what we're going to do with all this data and the insights we've started to identify.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **CLI Commands:** make (1)

#### Interpreting and communicating results
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interpreting-and-communicating-results?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interpreting-and-communicating-results?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] All right.
>
> **[0:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interpreting-and-communicating-results?u=76281980&t=1)** To wrap up this chapter on data analysis, I want to talk about how we can interpret the insights we're seeing and communicate the results of this analysis.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interpreting-and-communicating-results?u=76281980&t=8)** The next chapter is a deep dive into data visualizations and reporting, but excelling at these topics requires first, understanding how to communicate effectively to the stakeholders.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interpreting-and-communicating-results?u=76281980&t=19)** The first key point of this video is to understand what we're seeing from the techniques we have covered in this chapter.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interpreting-and-communicating-results?u=76281980&t=25)** We can start to see insights, patterns, and trends, but do we know what they mean?
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interpreting-and-communicating-results?u=76281980&t=32)** It's important to really think about the patterns we're seeing in the context of the original situation.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interpreting-and-communicating-results?u=76281980&t=38)** A common phrase in analysis is correlation doesn't mean causation, which means just because some metrics are correlated, as in we see a trend or a pattern emerging, doesn't mean that one caused the other.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interpreting-and-communicating-results?u=76281980&t=50)** Once we know what we're going to communicate, we need to next think about who we are communicating to.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interpreting-and-communicating-results?u=76281980&t=55)** Depending on who the people are, we'll decide how much technical details they'll want to know.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interpreting-and-communicating-results?u=76281980&t=63)** Usually, as you go up the management chain, folks are more interested in the patterns and what they can use them for, rather than the intricate details on statistical methods used to get the end result.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interpreting-and-communicating-results?u=76281980&t=74)** Another phrase I think fits well here is a picture is worth a thousand words.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interpreting-and-communicating-results?u=76281980&t=78)** Communicating with data visualizations, graphs, and charts can help to make the story much more clear as you explain the patterns and insights, which is why the next chapter is completely dedicated to reporting and data visualizations.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interpreting-and-communicating-results?u=76281980&t=92)** We've already touched on these a little to help us with our initial data analysis, but we are going to learn that we can derive even more value from our data.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interpreting-and-communicating-results?u=76281980&t=99)** See you in the next chapter.

#### Principles of effective data visualization
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/principles-of-effective-data-visualization?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/principles-of-effective-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] As we start to curate our data into visualizations for our business leaders, we need to think about some key principles to ensure we effectively communicate the correct story.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/principles-of-effective-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=11)** The first thing I think about when I start to create any reports or visualizations is to focus on communicating the key message.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/principles-of-effective-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=19)** With this in the forefront of my mind, I try to ensure that my visualizations are clear and simple.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/principles-of-effective-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=25)** They should be able to concisely portray the message.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/principles-of-effective-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=30)** This means that I need to choose the correct chart type for the data and the metrics that are being displayed.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/principles-of-effective-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=37)** The tools we use have so many options, so it's vitally important to understand which charts are best matches for our data sets.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/principles-of-effective-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=45)** Scales and axes are also worth considering ensuring that the graph can provide an accurate representation of the data.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/principles-of-effective-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=55)** Often people will manipulate charts in untruthful ways such to prove a point or for false advertising.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/principles-of-effective-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=62)** Examples of tampering with graphs include skewing the axes or by displaying multiple metrics on one graph, but using different axes.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/principles-of-effective-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=72)** Finally, keep the visualizations relevant to your target audience, who will view the graphs and charts or tell us how much detail is needed or maybe even which metrics to focus on.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/principles-of-effective-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=86)** Keeping these key principles of clarity, simplicity, accuracy, and relevance will ensure that you create data visualizations to effectively explain the data.

#### Data visualization tools and techniques

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-visualization-tools-and-techniques?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Now that we have the key principles under our belt, we can think about the tools we want to use to create our visualizations.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-visualization-tools-and-techniques?u=76281980&t=7)** Now, there are many options out there.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-visualization-tools-and-techniques?u=76281980&t=10)** I'm just going to mention a few of what I consider to be the most popular tools.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-visualization-tools-and-techniques?u=76281980&t=15)** However, I'll place a special focus on what we're looking for in a data visualization tool.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-visualization-tools-and-techniques?u=76281980&t=21)** It's possible you'll find other tools along the way that might fit your needs better, but the concepts and features will be similar to what we'll see here.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-visualization-tools-and-techniques?u=76281980&t=30)** So how do we choose a tool?
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-visualization-tools-and-techniques?u=76281980&t=32)** Simply put, we need to find one where the features offered, match up with the requirements that we have.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-visualization-tools-and-techniques?u=76281980&t=39)** Think about what your requirements are as we walk through these four criteria to help us choose a tool.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-visualization-tools-and-techniques?u=76281980&t=47)** The first requirement to think about is ease of use.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-visualization-tools-and-techniques?u=76281980&t=50)** Depending on who is building the visualizations and their levels of skill, it will determine which tool is best for the job.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-visualization-tools-and-techniques?u=76281980&t=58)** Tools such as Microsoft Excel or Google Sheets are perfect for users that are less technical.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-visualization-tools-and-techniques?u=76281980&t=65)** Most businesses already use a spreadsheet tool, so these are readily available and can be connected to many different data sources.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-visualization-tools-and-techniques?u=76281980&t=74)** The second requirement is scalability.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-visualization-tools-and-techniques?u=76281980&t=77)** We already know that our data sets can get really vast, so we need to make sure that the tool chosen is up to the job.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-visualization-tools-and-techniques?u=76281980&t=84)** Tools like Excel or Sheets will start to struggle after a certain point.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-visualization-tools-and-techniques?u=76281980&t=89)** And so moving on to looking at either Power BI or Tableau, which are specifically designed to handle this workload, is usually a good option.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-visualization-tools-and-techniques?u=76281980&t=99)** Third, we want to think about flexibility and customization of our data visualizations.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-visualization-tools-and-techniques?u=76281980&t=105)** Again, tools like Power BI and Tableau offer a lot more options here since they are specifically designed for the job.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-visualization-tools-and-techniques?u=76281980&t=114)** Finally, we need to consider whether the tools can be easily integrated into our existing systems.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-visualization-tools-and-techniques?u=76281980&t=120)** Being able to easily pull data from existing databases, data warehouses, or data lakes can greatly enhance our ability to create useful reports.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-visualization-tools-and-techniques?u=76281980&t=130)** You can use the Notebook feature under the course player to jot down your requirements needed from a tool.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-visualization-tools-and-techniques?u=76281980&t=136)** You can come back to these requirements as you're planning your overall data management strategy.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-visualization-tools-and-techniques?u=76281980&t=143)** Whichever tool you use, it's best to use data that is clean and well-prepared.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-visualization-tools-and-techniques?u=76281980&t=148)** Since we've worked through the rest of the data management lifecycle, we should now have the data we need for visualizations readily available.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-visualization-tools-and-techniques?u=76281980&t=157)** Tools like Power BI and Tableau can however be used to manipulate the data and create measures or metrics off of the dataset, which can then be used in your reports.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-visualization-tools-and-techniques?u=76281980&t=169)** These tools can also bring together data from other sources.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-visualization-tools-and-techniques?u=76281980&t=172)** If you aren't reporting off of a data warehouse that has already had third-party data integrated, you could do that at this stage.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/data-visualization-tools-and-techniques?u=76281980&t=180)** Once you have your tool of choice selected, you'll be ready to create dashboards and reports that help tell the story of the data and aid the business leaders with making decisions off of the data we've collected and curated.

#### Dashboard design and development
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/dashboard-design-and-development?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/dashboard-design-and-development?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] A dashboard is a visual display of key metrics that provides an at a glance view into a topic.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/dashboard-design-and-development?u=76281980&t=6)** This topic could be the overall company performance or perhaps a view into how a specific process is working.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/dashboard-design-and-development?u=76281980&t=13)** In order for the dashboard to be useful, it needs to be designed in a way that allows people to look at it and immediately process the information and to be able to make decisions based on what is presented.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/dashboard-design-and-development?u=76281980&t=26)** Metrics should be grouped into logical sets and there should be a flow as you read through from top left to bottom right.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/dashboard-design-and-development?u=76281980&t=33)** We also want to ensure that the dashboard is not overcrowded with too many charts and graphs in a single visualization.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/dashboard-design-and-development?u=76281980&t=41)** Making use of white space will enable the viewer to better focus their eyes on important information.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/dashboard-design-and-development?u=76281980&t=48)** Also, consider the type of visualizations you use.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/dashboard-design-and-development?u=76281980&t=52)** Certain graphs and charts are better for certain purposes, so make sure that you take this into consideration to ensure the dashboard is clear and concise.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/dashboard-design-and-development?u=76281980&t=63)** Dashboards also have the option of adding interactive elements, perhaps a slider to control the date or timeframe and view where all the visualizations will reflect this change in scope.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/dashboard-design-and-development?u=76281980&t=73)** We'll dig into that in the next video.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/dashboard-design-and-development?u=76281980&t=78)** Finally, think about branding and style.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/dashboard-design-and-development?u=76281980&t=80)** As you create more dashboards, it's important to maintain a consistent look and feel.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/dashboard-design-and-development?u=76281980&t=86)** Work to create smart looking dashboards, so users may easily find their way to finding and viewing different dashboards.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/dashboard-design-and-development?u=76281980&t=94)** Also, consider accessibility.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/dashboard-design-and-development?u=76281980&t=97)** As you're designing your dashboard, you can use color theory to distinguish between your data points, but also make sure to use a palette that is colorblind friendly.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/dashboard-design-and-development?u=76281980&t=110)** So far, we've covered dashboard design from the point of view of what the user will see.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/dashboard-design-and-development?u=76281980&t=115)** However, we also need to consider performance.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/dashboard-design-and-development?u=76281980&t=119)** As we're loading or refreshing the dashboard, we need to optimize the way we retrieve data from the source, potentially a database.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/dashboard-design-and-development?u=76281980&t=127)** If the queries that gather the data take a long time to execute, it's going to negatively impact the user experience.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/dashboard-design-and-development?u=76281980&t=135)** If you're pulling data from a large spreadsheet, ensure you only have the data you really need.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/dashboard-design-and-development?u=76281980&t=141)** On the other hand, if you're writing T-SQL queries to pull data from a SQL Server database, make sure they are written in a way that is as performant as possible.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/dashboard-design-and-development?u=76281980&t=151)** There are many data sources available, so how you optimize will vary depending on them, but these are a couple of considerations to keep in mind.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/dashboard-design-and-development?u=76281980&t=161)** We can also consider caching data if it doesn't need to be refreshed that often, perhaps part of the dashboard is showing more historic data that could be refreshed daily, and then cached to speed up report loading times.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/dashboard-design-and-development?u=76281980&t=176)** Creating the perfect dashboard is part science and part art.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/dashboard-design-and-development?u=76281980&t=180)** It's worth digging deeper into UX or user experience design to learn more on how to use these principles to create the perfect dashboard to not only display data, but to aid with making decisions.

#### Interactive data visualization
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interactive-data-visualization?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interactive-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Often when we think about reporting, we think about static reports that show a specific timeframe and lack interactivity.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interactive-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=9)** In this video, we'll focus on how more interactive reports and dashboards can be used to dig into the data and get at those key insights.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interactive-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=18)** Being able to interact with the data gives the users power to move around as they please and drill down into the details.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interactive-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=28)** Interactive elements could include sliders to change the date, which affects all of the visuals on the dashboard.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interactive-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=35)** This means that we could be viewing data over a 24-hour period, which would allow us to see peaks at certain hours.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interactive-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=42)** Most tools will allow us to highlight this area and refocus the dashboard to drill into this more specific timeframe.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interactive-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=51)** The dashboard could also include filters that can change what data is shown, again, affecting all visuals on the page.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interactive-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=58)** This allows us to filter by customer demographics or perhaps product categories so you can turn dull data into a more engaging data story.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interactive-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=69)** These interactive elements allow users to access the exact data they want but still in a curated and somewhat controlled fashion.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interactive-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=78)** This will enable users to see patterns at a macro level and then drill down into the details to try and find out why the data is shaped in that certain way.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interactive-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=88)** It's also worth mentioning that we can also add tooltips to help explain the graphics and the data that is displayed.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interactive-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=96)** Hovering over certain areas of a chart, for example, could show you the specifics of what's being shown.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interactive-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=103)** Having this displayed for all categories by default would clutter the dashboard and make it harder to read, but by utilizing tooltips, the information is there if it's needed without causing too much noise and overwhelming the viewer.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interactive-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=119)** Dashboards can also utilize real-time data to provide an instant look into certain metrics.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interactive-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=125)** Data such as website traffic or sales can be monitored in real time to allow the business to react in an agile fashion, perhaps scaling up infrastructure to meet demands and avoid website issues or by offering promos to certain customers.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interactive-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=141)** Not all of the people that view your dashboards are going to want to see the exact same view.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interactive-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=146)** Interactive dashboards could also be customized depending on who's logged in, perhaps changing what's displayed or how it's displayed.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interactive-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=154)** An example would be the option to choose a theme, such as a light or dark mode, to view the dashboard in.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/interactive-data-visualization?u=76281980&t=162)** Thoughtfully designed, interactive dashboards can provide a very useful tool for people throughout the business to monitor certain processes or for business leaders to drill into overall company performance.

#### Storytelling with data
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/storytelling-with-data?u=76281980)

>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/storytelling-with-data?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Let's talk about data storytelling.
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/storytelling-with-data?u=76281980&t=3)** It's about building a narrative from our data visualizations.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/storytelling-with-data?u=76281980&t=7)** As you've seen from the videos in this chapter, we are building dashboards, and reports for people outside of the data team.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/storytelling-with-data?u=76281980&t=14)** These folks want to be able to view the graphics, and understand the story that is being told from the data.
>

>

>

>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/storytelling-with-data?u=76281980&t=82)** Who was studied or where the data was gathered.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/storytelling-with-data?u=76281980&t=86)** Plot.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/storytelling-with-data?u=76281980&t=87)** This connects the data points to tell the overall story.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/storytelling-with-data?u=76281980&t=91)** Conflict.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/storytelling-with-data?u=76281980&t=92)** Which could relate to a change from the expected, such as a decrease in revenue.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/storytelling-with-data?u=76281980&t=97)** And finally, resolution, which is where you will describe your findings.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/storytelling-with-data?u=76281980&t=103)** As you build together the story from these elements, you should include data that tells the story of the narrative in an unbiased fashion.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/storytelling-with-data?u=76281980&t=111)** It should be arranged in a way that makes it easy to follow, and provide credibility to the story that's being told.

#### Reporting best practices
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/reporting-best-practices?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/reporting-best-practices?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] To wrap up this chapter on reporting and data visualizations, I'll be highlighting some best practices.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/reporting-best-practices?u=76281980&t=6)** Then, in the next video of the chapter, I'll highlight some common challenges.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/reporting-best-practices?u=76281980&t=10)** I believe these two videos will set you up to succeed in this area.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/reporting-best-practices?u=76281980&t=16)** The first and I think the most important best practice is to focus on clarity and simplicity, making use of white space to ensure that reports or dashboards don't look cluttered and keeping the language, axes, and design simple.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/reporting-best-practices?u=76281980&t=31)** Our aim is to portray the key insights without overloading the person viewing the report.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/reporting-best-practices?u=76281980&t=38)** Secondly, know your audience.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/reporting-best-practices?u=76281980&t=40)** The report should be tailored to what they need to know.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/reporting-best-practices?u=76281980&t=44)** Are they the top leaders of your company that care about high-level summaries or are we targeting individual contributors who need to know the ins and outs of a certain process?
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/reporting-best-practices?u=76281980&t=56)** Focus on choosing the right charts and graphs for the right data, ensuring that the visualization clearly communicates the message.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/reporting-best-practices?u=76281980&t=65)** Ensure that you are highlighting the key insights and actionable data.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/reporting-best-practices?u=76281980&t=70)** Folks reading this report want to know what the data is showing but also want the report to show why and what that means for the business.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/reporting-best-practices?u=76281980&t=79)** Also, as far as the design, make sure it's on-brand.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/reporting-best-practices?u=76281980&t=83)** You may ask if the company has branded templates for business use.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/reporting-best-practices?u=76281980&t=87)** This also helps to create continuity between reports, as people are looking through many.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/reporting-best-practices?u=76281980&t=94)** Again, think about accessibility in the design phase.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/reporting-best-practices?u=76281980&t=97)** Ensure a color palette that is friendly to color deficiencies and add alt text for any images or graphs to ensure people using screen readers can read your reports.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/reporting-best-practices?u=76281980&t=108)** This is an ongoing process.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/reporting-best-practices?u=76281980&t=111)** Once you create these perfectly clear reports and publish them for all to see, it's not over.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/reporting-best-practices?u=76281980&t=117)** You need to continually revisit the reports and ensure that they are still following these best practices.
>

>

>

>

>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/reporting-best-practices?u=76281980&t=144)** Well, you can schedule the report so that it automatically gathers the latest data and gets delivered to her inbox at 6:25 so it's ready for action.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/reporting-best-practices?u=76281980&t=154)** These best practices will help you to succeed in creating reports off of the data we've collected.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/reporting-best-practices?u=76281980&t=159)** And this is a really important step.
>

#### Common data visualization challenges
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/common-data-visualization-challenges?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/common-data-visualization-challenges?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] In the previous video, we talked about best practices.
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/common-data-visualization-challenges?u=76281980&t=3)** Now, we are going to talk about common challenges.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/common-data-visualization-challenges?u=76281980&t=6)** You'll notice these are basically the inverse of our best practices, and if we can avoid these pitfalls, we'll have some excellent data visualizations to show off.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/common-data-visualization-challenges?u=76281980&t=17)** One common challenge is overcomplicating things.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/common-data-visualization-challenges?u=76281980&t=21)** By adding too many visuals to a report or too many notes and annotations to a specific chart, we can make things overcrowded and hard to understand.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/common-data-visualization-challenges?u=76281980&t=32)** We'll also want to make sure our colors are used in moderation.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/common-data-visualization-challenges?u=76281980&t=35)** Keep on brand, but make sure the palette used is easy on the eyes, friendly to any color deficiencies, and fits together well.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/common-data-visualization-challenges?u=76281980&t=45)** The biggest thing we want to avoid though is to create misleading visuals.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/common-data-visualization-challenges?u=76281980&t=50)** An example of this is using scale inappropriately or manipulating axes so the charts show skewed data in a way that leads the person reading it to improper conclusions.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/common-data-visualization-challenges?u=76281980&t=61)** Our graphs should display the data in a way that makes it easy to read and the representation is true.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/common-data-visualization-challenges?u=76281980&t=69)** Chart type choices can also cause challenges.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/common-data-visualization-challenges?u=76281980&t=72)** We spoke about the importance of choosing the right chart for the right data set.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/common-data-visualization-challenges?u=76281980&t=77)** This is often something that goes wrong as folks start to put dashboards and reports together without considering whether the chart type is a good choice for the dataset.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/common-data-visualization-challenges?u=76281980&t=86)** Remember, we want to make this as clear as we can for the benefit of our readers.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/common-data-visualization-challenges?u=76281980&t=93)** Which leads me onto the next common pitfall, ignoring our audience's needs and requirements.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/common-data-visualization-challenges?u=76281980&t=99)** We really need to consider the target audience, making sure that they can get the information they need from our reports.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/common-data-visualization-challenges?u=76281980&t=109)** If we provide too much information and too much granular data to our executive team, they are not going to get what they need from our report, and they'll probably just stop using it.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/common-data-visualization-challenges?u=76281980&t=120)** The granular detailed reports need to be created specifically for the people that can make use of that data.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/common-data-visualization-challenges?u=76281980&t=127)** Whereas for our execs, they want a high level summary that answers the questions they care about.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/common-data-visualization-challenges?u=76281980&t=134)** If you can avoid these common pitfalls, you'll be in great shape to create some really useful visuals that will benefit the business.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/common-data-visualization-challenges?u=76281980&t=143)** The final step in this data management lifecycle is the presentation layer, and so it's important we do this well so we can display all the hard work we've put into sourcing, cleaning, and curating the perfect data for our organization.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>

### 7. Data Governance and Compliance

> [[#Table of Contents|↑ Back to Table of Contents]]

#### Introduction to data governance
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-governance?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-governance?u=76281980&t=0)** - So far, we've focused on the main stages of our data management lifecycle, and now it's time to move on to the supporting topics which surround our whole process.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-governance?u=76281980&t=9)** Welcome to the data governance chapter.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-governance?u=76281980&t=11)** First off, what is data governance?
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-governance?u=76281980&t=14)** This is a framework for managing our data and ensuring it is accurate, reliable, and secure.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-governance?u=76281980&t=21)** We will talk about how we can establish data policies and standards to govern how data is handled and how data management processes should be carried out.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-governance?u=76281980&t=31)** These policies will help us to ensure we meet any regulatory and compliance requirements that apply to our data, either from a location or an industry perspective.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-governance?u=76281980&t=40)** Data privacy is also a huge topic which we'll dedicate a whole video to.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-governance?u=76281980&t=46)** As we collect customer and employee data, we have a responsibility to handle it in a certain fashion.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-governance?u=76281980&t=51)** I'm sure that you yourself have been notified by companies in the past that there has been a data breach and some of your data has been stolen; that's a terrible feeling and one we want to ensure we avoid for our customers.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-governance?u=76281980&t=64)** There are certain data security frameworks that we can follow to gain recognition, but also ensure we're following best practices and doing everything we can from a security standpoint.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-governance?u=76281980&t=76)** We will also discuss access control.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-governance?u=76281980&t=78)** Not everyone in your organization needs access to all of the data.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-governance?u=76281980&t=84)** Locking this down and granting access using the principle of least privilege will help to ensure our data is safe.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-governance?u=76281980&t=92)** The principle of least privilege is a concept which states: users should have the minimum required permissions in order to complete their task.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-governance?u=76281980&t=100)** For example, users that only need to read data should not have access to write or change that data.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-governance?u=76281980&t=109)** Finally, this isn't a once-and-done kind of step.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/introduction-to-data-governance?u=76281980&t=111)** We need to be continuously monitoring for suspicious activity and auditing to ensure we're following the standards and procedures that we've put in place.

>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/establishing-data-policies-standards?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Presenter] As we start to talk about data governance, our first stop is to discuss policies and standards.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/establishing-data-policies-standards?u=76281980&t=7)** This may sound less interesting than some of the other topics we've covered so far, but they are vital in ensuring our data is secure and safe.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/establishing-data-policies-standards?u=76281980&t=17)** Policies are high-level rules that tell us how our data should be managed, accessed, and protected.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/establishing-data-policies-standards?u=76281980&t=24)** It's important to work through what policies should be and make them available to all employees in your organization.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/establishing-data-policies-standards?u=76281980&t=32)** It's one thing to have policies, but the important thing is to make sure you're following them.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/establishing-data-policies-standards?u=76281980&t=40)** Data standards go hand in hand with these policies.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/establishing-data-policies-standards?u=76281980&t=43)** These are more specific though, and relate to how we standardize our data and ensure it is accurate and reliable.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/establishing-data-policies-standards?u=76281980&t=51)** These could be naming standards or perhaps standards for the format data should be stored in.

>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/establishing-data-policies-standards?u=76281980&t=74)** If a lot of your data management is going to be in Azure, I'd strongly recommend reviewing this resource, especially the Govern section.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/establishing-data-policies-standards?u=76281980&t=84)** A couple of examples of policies could be a data access policy.

>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/establishing-data-policies-standards?u=76281980&t=95)** It's also important to state how long permissions are granted and how this access will be monitored and reviewed.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/establishing-data-policies-standards?u=76281980&t=103)** Another example could be data retention policies.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/establishing-data-policies-standards?u=76281980&t=107)** We mentioned this earlier in the course.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/establishing-data-policies-standards?u=76281980&t=109)** We don't want to keep all the data forever.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/establishing-data-policies-standards?u=76281980&t=112)** This is going to increase our storage and resource costs to process that data, but it also increases our risk of poor security and potential breach.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/establishing-data-policies-standards?u=76281980&t=124)** We want to categorize data and ensure retention periods are in place and closely followed so that we're only keeping the data we really need.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/establishing-data-policies-standards?u=76281980&t=136)** Creating and enforcing policies and standards can be a lot of work, but it's important for a number of reasons.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/establishing-data-policies-standards?u=76281980&t=144)** It ensures we're in compliance for any regulatory requirements.
>

>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/establishing-data-policies-standards?u=76281980&t=150)** It ensures our data quality is high, and we know how important that is throughout our data management lifecycle.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/establishing-data-policies-standards?u=76281980&t=158)** They improve our data security and protect us from potential breaches, and it improves efficiency.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/establishing-data-policies-standards?u=76281980&t=166)** If there are agreed upon policies in place, all we have to do is follow them.

> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/establishing-data-policies-standards?u=76281980&t=170)** No need for lengthy discussions every year when you're trying to decide if data should be removed.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/establishing-data-policies-standards?u=76281980&t=177)** The data retention policy says data will be kept for five years.

#### Regulatory compliance requirements
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/regulatory-compliance-requirements?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/regulatory-compliance-requirements?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] The data policies and standards we talked about in the previous video are vital in keeping our data safe and our organization in a good place, but one step further from those policies are regulatory requirements.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/regulatory-compliance-requirements?u=76281980&t=15)** Now, the policies can help us to ensure we meet these requirements, but there are financial penalties and damage to our reputation if we are not compliant with any requirements that apply to us.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/regulatory-compliance-requirements?u=76281980&t=26)** These regulatory requirements could apply to us based on the geographic location that the company operates in or the industry and the type of data that it handles.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/regulatory-compliance-requirements?u=76281980&t=37)** Either way, it's important to recognize all the regulations you need to follow, and then ensure you have policies and standards in place to make it so.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/regulatory-compliance-requirements?u=76281980&t=48)** One location-based regulatory framework is GDPR, the General Data Protection Regulation.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/regulatory-compliance-requirements?u=76281980&t=55)** This protects the data of EU citizens, and there are strict requirements on the data you can collect and store.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/regulatory-compliance-requirements?u=76281980&t=64)** A more industry-specific example of a regulatory framework is HIPAA, the Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/regulatory-compliance-requirements?u=76281980&t=73)** This is a law in the USA for ensuring the safety of health-related data.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/regulatory-compliance-requirements?u=76281980&t=82)** These regulatory frameworks can be different as far as what they require, but there are often some common themes.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/regulatory-compliance-requirements?u=76281980&t=90)** These include data privacy, or how we protect personal or sensitive data, data security, whether data should be encrypted and who should have access, data retention, how long data should be kept.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/regulatory-compliance-requirements?u=76281980&t=106)** This can be broken into many different retention periods depending on the kind of data we're storing.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/regulatory-compliance-requirements?u=76281980&t=111)** And incident response.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/regulatory-compliance-requirements?u=76281980&t=113)** This is how we respond if there is a breach or a security incident.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/regulatory-compliance-requirements?u=76281980&t=117)** Who should be notified and in what timeframe the response needs to occur.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/regulatory-compliance-requirements?u=76281980&t=123)** Compliance with these regulations is vital though.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/regulatory-compliance-requirements?u=76281980&t=126)** For example, at the time of writing this course, severe violations of GDPR can cost up to 20 million euros or 4% of total global turnover, whichever is higher.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/regulatory-compliance-requirements?u=76281980&t=139)** That's a serious amount of money.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/regulatory-compliance-requirements?u=76281980&t=145)** Getting caught not meeting regulations can also impact your company's reputation and brand.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/regulatory-compliance-requirements?u=76281980&t=151)** Customers will be wary of dealing with companies that have had issues here.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/regulatory-compliance-requirements?u=76281980&t=156)** Staying in compliance with regulatory requirements is a big undertaking, but it's so important.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-management-essential-training/regulatory-compliance-requirements?u=76281980&t=162)** Make sure you spend enough time and energy on this topic to ensure you understand your specific requirements and that you have the policies in place to remain compliant.
